<h3><a name="page-1157395">CB06_0166</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='166'>166</span></p>
<p>Mch 13<sup>th</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>B. Sargent Briggs Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I find that I have<span class='line-break'> </span>on hand steps which can be altered<span class='line-break'> </span>over and also some plain buttresses<span class='line-break'> </span>all of Rockport granite.</p>
<p>The steps would be six or seven in<span class='line-break'> </span>number and then to three &amp; one half<span class='line-break'> </span>ft wide &amp; the buttresses very plain.</p>
<p>They would require more or less<span class='line-break'> </span>alteration &amp; recutting &amp; I could not<span class='line-break'> </span>put them up for less than $60.<span class='line-break'> </span>If you want your name or the<span class='line-break'> </span>number of the lot cut on them that<span class='line-break'> </span>would be additional according to the<span class='line-break'> </span>kind of letter. Raised letters thick<span class='line-break'> </span>one half inch high from $2.<sup>00 </sup>to $2.<sup>50</sup> each.</p>
<p>I don't know whether you would<span class='line-break'> </span>not do as such to go directly to a<span class='line-break'> </span>stone cutter - that you mentioned.</p>
<p>Ys very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>JW. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157404">CB06_0175</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='175'>175</span></p>
<p>April 7<sup>th</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>D.W. Hitchcock Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The land about<span class='line-break'> </span>which you inquire yesterday, has<span class='line-break'> </span>not been offered for sale in lots<span class='line-break'> </span>as it is desirable to keep some open<span class='line-break'> </span>land near the front entrance and<span class='line-break'> </span>as a drain passes across it some 9 or<span class='line-break'> </span>10 feet below the surface, as shown<span class='line-break'> </span>by the enclosed plan on which a new<span class='line-break'> </span>lot has been laid out, next to that<span class='line-break'> </span>last sold (no #3891). This new lot (not <span class='line-break'> </span>numbered on plan) contains 300 sq.<span class='line-break'> </span>ft.</p>
<p>If this lot were sold at all, it would<span class='line-break'> </span>be with the understanding that no<span class='line-break'> </span>stonework other than monuments, headstones<span class='line-break'> </span>or the corner posts set by the Corporation to<span class='line-break'> </span>mark the lot, be placed there.</p>
<p>The drain is very substantialy built<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; covered with heavy stone &amp; would<span class='line-break'> </span>be several feet below any burial<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; would I believe do no damage to<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot, but I should want you<span class='line-break'> </span>if you bought the lot to understand that<span class='line-break'> </span>there was a drain there.</p>
<p>The price of the lot, marked with the<span class='line-break'> </span>corner posts as set by the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>and with the turfing under perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care would be $1500.</p>
<p>There are numerous lots in other parts<span class='line-break'> </span>of the cemetery which as lots, are quite<span class='line-break'> </span>as desirable, which I could sell you<span class='line-break'> </span>for considerably less.</p>
<p>Ys very truly <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1157407">
<h3><a name="page-1157407">CB06_0178</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='178'>178</span></p>
<p>The gardening work for the season of 1882 will be ar<span class='line-break'></span>ranged as follows</p>
<p>The care of lots will be taken by six sections<span class='line-break'> </span>of work according to the plans &amp; books furnished at the<span class='line-break'> </span>outset to the tickets afterwards sent out.</p>
<p>The Sections will contain approximately the following<span class='line-break'> </span>number of lots.</p>
<p>N<sup>o</sup> 1-559 lots: N<sup>o</sup> 2-526; N<sup>o</sup> 3-399; N<sup>o</sup> 4- 438.<span class='line-break'> </span>N<sup>o</sup> 5-[44?] ; N<sup>o</sup> 6-399</p>
<p>All lots on the section books whether staked or not are<span class='line-break'> </span>to be cared for, but no other lots are to be cared for<span class='line-break'> </span>without a ticket from office.</p>
<p>No corrections of any kind are to be made in the section<span class='line-break'> </span>books by the Gardener or his men, but all mistakes report<span class='line-break'></span>ed promptly at the office by the section foreman.</p>
<p>The Gardener will direct his section foreman to bring<span class='line-break'> </span>in their books to the office every Tuesday noon without<span class='line-break'> </span>fail.</p>
<p>The Stone Farm Section will to be [?] of the lots sold or</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157408">
<h3><a name="page-1157408">CB06_0179</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='179'>179</span></p>
<p>vacant between Swan &amp; Eagle, Eagle Pearl &amp; Crystal,<span class='line-break'> </span>the circle and the Coolidge lot on Swan Avenue, but<span class='line-break'> </span>will not as heretofore take any care of the paths or<span class='line-break'> </span>avenues beyond edging them.</p>
<p>The front borders of all neglected lots on avenues and<span class='line-break'> </span>paths are to be cut as often as necessary by the section men.<span class='line-break'> </span>Lawn movers as well as sickles will hereafter be left for [?]<span class='line-break'> </span>pairs at the Engine house - Men will wait for repairs, but<span class='line-break'> </span>will leave their mower &amp; exchange for another.</p>
<p>Particular attention is called to the printed notice on the<span class='line-break'> </span>section hand carts.</p>
<p>The rubbish made by the Jobbers must be more promptly<span class='line-break'> </span>cleaned than in past season.</p>
<p>No changes to be made on any ticket for plants or<span class='line-break'> </span>other work or other work except at the office - nor is<span class='line-break'> </span>any work to be done by the Gardener or his men until<span class='line-break'> </span>the ticket for the same has been given out from the office,<span class='line-break'> </span>except that in cases which do not admit of delay,<span class='line-break'> </span>the Gardener may communicate with the Supt's office by<span class='line-break'> </span>the telephone and make arrangements for doing the<span class='line-break'> </span>work at once.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157409">
<h3><a name="page-1157409">CB06_0180</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='180'>180</span></p>
<p>In all cases where proprietors desire to change<span class='line-break'> </span>their orders for plants or other work, the gardener is<span class='line-break'> </span>particularly instructed to get an order for the work, as<span class='line-break'> </span>ticket will not be issued on verbal instructions to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Gardener or others.</p>
<p>The ornamental Sections will have the care, weeding,<span class='line-break'> </span>watering, edging &amp; training of all plants, shrubs &amp;c in<span class='line-break'> </span>the ornamental beds including those on the Stone Farm beds<span class='line-break'> </span>but the grass will be cut by a special section as ordered<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Supt.</p>
<p>The gardener will account on his weekly report for<span class='line-break'> </span>the time of all the men, sent him by the Supt. -<span class='line-break'> </span>The gardener will reduce the force at the Greenhouse to<span class='line-break'> </span>two men after June 1, until otherwise directed by the Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157410">
<h3><a name="page-1157410">CB06_0181</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='181'>181</span></p>
<p>Apl 15th [18]82</p>
<p>Mrs S.B. Johnson<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>In regard to your inquiries at<span class='line-break'> </span>the Boston office as to the progress of the work on your<span class='line-break'> </span>lot. I find that part of the work is done but the<span class='line-break'> </span>sodding part had to be delayed untill the season<span class='line-break'> </span>advanced far enough to get sods. The work to be done<span class='line-break'> </span>is I think perfectly understood between us and I think<span class='line-break'> </span>you will find it satisfactory when furnished.</p>
<p>I notice Messrs O'Brien &amp; Son have taken<span class='line-break'> </span>out a permit to care for the lot for the coming season.<span class='line-break'> </span>Where we sod a lot we care for it for that season without<span class='line-break'> </span>extra charge and as we are responsible for the sods for that<span class='line-break'> </span>time we prefer to do it. If you desire us to be responsible<span class='line-break'> </span>for the condition of the sod after the work is finished, I should<span class='line-break'> </span>with to have the entire charge of the lot for the season.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>

<p>Apl 24th [18]82</p>
<p>Horace N. &amp; John H. Fisher Esqr.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sirs</p>
<p>Last year I found that the caring<span class='line-break'> </span>for you family lot for only half the season worked<span class='line-break'> </span>unsatisfactorly. Certainly the lot suffered and begin<span class='line-break'></span>-ing work on it at the season we did it was a losing<span class='line-break'> </span>job for the Corporation - If you will give the order<span class='line-break'> </span>now it will be charged $15 for the season for the<span class='line-break'> </span>whole 2816 ft. <div id="page-1157421">
<h3><a name="page-1157421">CB06_0192</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='192'>192</span></p>
<p>Apl 25th [18]82</p>
<p>J.J. Horgan Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridgeport</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your note received. I think you<span class='line-break'> </span>have done sufficient work in Mt Auburn to know<span class='line-break'> </span>that our rule is that foundations must go to the<span class='line-break'> </span>bottom of the grave. There have been so many<span class='line-break'> </span>cases of caving that a foundation that does not<span class='line-break'> </span>go so deep is of no practical use. If you had left<span class='line-break'> </span>the root of those stones as deep as the foundations should<span class='line-break'> </span>be there would have been no trouble. Knowing our<span class='line-break'> </span>rules as to foundations it seems to me you could have<span class='line-break'> </span>included that in you estimate or if you had any<span class='line-break'> </span>doubt about it you could have asked the cost before hand<span class='line-break'> </span>as stonecutters repeatedly do.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1157425">CB06_0196</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='196'>196</span></p>
<p>May 1st [188]2</p>
<p>Hon. J.M. Clark</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>My estimate for<span class='line-break'> </span>repairing the curbing around your<span class='line-break'> </span>lot (No 3337 Laurel Ave is as<span class='line-break'> </span>follows.<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>14 iron clamps galvanized</th> <th>$3.50<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>6 days masons &amp; cutting &amp; clamp'g</td> <td>18.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>1 <sup>1</sup>/3 [days] leading joints</td> <td>4.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>50 lts lead</td> <td>3.50</td> </tr> <tr><td>1 <sup>1</sup>/2 labor sodding, borders &amp; next curb'g</td> <td>3.37</td> </tr> <tr><td>120 ft sods</td> <td>3.60</td> </tr> <tr><td>[Total]</td> <td>$35.97</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> The cost of a stone post if wanted<span class='line-break'> </span>for the vase you propose to place on the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot would be $3.50 to $5.00 set, according<span class='line-break'> </span>to whether a post 10" square would answer,<span class='line-break'> </span>or whether a larger one must be put there<span class='line-break'> </span>say 12 inches square, which is probably as<span class='line-break'> </span>large as any I now have on hand.</p>
<p>The open joint could be filled with<span class='line-break'> </span>lead at a smaller expense, but the<span class='line-break'> </span>curb unless clamped &amp; reset would<span class='line-break'> </span>continue to move with each winter's frost<span class='line-break'> </span>so that while the first cost would be<span class='line-break'> </span>less, it would in my opinion be poor<span class='line-break'> </span>economy to repair in that way.</p>
<p>The flower will be placed in the<span class='line-break'> </span>vase as you request instead of in<span class='line-break'> </span>the borders.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt .</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157426">CB06_0197</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='197'>197</span></p>
<p>May 2nd [18]82</p>
<p>Miss Caroline Tewksbury<span class='line-break'> </span>Lynn, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>Your postal card received ordering<span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle planted in your lot #587. I think it best to explain<span class='line-break'> </span>to you that myrtle is planted in perpetual care lots only<span class='line-break'> </span>under perpetual care. That is if a myrtle grave is<span class='line-break'> </span>ordered in an ordinary lot the charge is $7 for planting<span class='line-break'> </span>the myrtle and caring for it one year but if the lot is<span class='line-break'> </span>under perpetual care (as yours is) $17 is the charge and<span class='line-break'> </span>for that sum the corporation keeps the myrtle on grave<span class='line-break'> </span>in good condition for ever. The charge for the two graves<span class='line-break'> </span>would therefore be $34.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1157439">CB06_0210</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='210'>210</span></p>
<p>#2917</p>
<p>May 17 [18]82</p>
<p>Freeman J Doe Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In regard to your letter to our Treasurer March 17th<span class='line-break'> </span>I find it impossible to make any permanent improvem<span class='line-break'></span>-ent to the paths unless the curbing is reset. I would<span class='line-break'> </span>advise you to have the stone work reset, secured with<span class='line-break'> </span>clamps, leaded and cleaned. This with sodding where<span class='line-break'> </span>needed will cost $31.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1157440">CB06_0211</a></h3>

<p>#2929</p>
<p>May 18 [18]82</p>

<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>I have examined your lot and<span class='line-break'> </span>find that to build foundations under 4 headstones,<span class='line-break'> </span>clean marble, remove fence, grade and sod lot will<span class='line-break'> </span>cost $22 and the old material of fence.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157441">CB06_0212</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='212'>212</span></p>
<p>May 18 [18]82</p>
<p>George L Andrews<span class='line-break'> </span>West Point N.Y.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have examined the marble plinth<span class='line-break'> </span>of headstone marked mother in lot #1466. It looks as<span class='line-break'> </span>if it would last for 3 or 4 years yet. When it becomes<span class='line-break'> </span>unsightly it will have to be replaced (repair being impossible)<span class='line-break'> </span>A stonecutter is the proper party to attend to that matter.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<div id="page-1157443">
<h3><a name="page-1157443">CB06_0214</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='214'>214</span></p>
<p>May 19<sup>th</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>Miss Sarah Dunn</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>Your note with<span class='line-break'> </span>reference to lot #1943 has been received<span class='line-break'> </span>and shall have prompt attention.</p>
<p>The graves in the rear of the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>have settled very considerably and<span class='line-break'> </span>of course the myrtle has settled with<span class='line-break'> </span>them. This generally occurs after a time<span class='line-break'> </span>unless the burials are made in brick<span class='line-break'> </span>vaults, and the only way to do will be<span class='line-break'> </span>to take up all the myrtle &amp; fill in<span class='line-break'> </span>considerable earth &amp; then replant<span class='line-break'> </span>the myrtle. As the myrtle will not look<span class='line-break'> </span>as well after replanting, until it<span class='line-break'> </span>has had time to make some new<span class='line-break'> </span>growth. I would like to hear form<span class='line-break'> </span>you before doing anything, as you<span class='line-break'> </span>may prefer not to have this done<span class='line-break'> </span>at present.</p>
<p>One of the headstones has settled<span class='line-break'> </span>too, and should be reset. There does<span class='line-break'> </span>not appear to be any foundations<span class='line-break'> </span>under it.</p>
<p>The whole cost of raising the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>in the back, &amp; resetting the myrtle &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>raising the headstone &amp; putting a foun<span class='line-break'></span>dation under it would be $10.<sup>00</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>It may be that a foundation will<span class='line-break'> </span>not be needed, which would reduce<span class='line-break'> </span>the expense some four dollars, but this<span class='line-break'> </span>can be seen better when the stone is<span class='line-break'> </span>reset. This work can be done next week<span class='line-break'> </span>if you will advise us promptly.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt<span class='line-break'> </span>214</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>May 20th [18]82</p>

<p>Your note received. We can set the<span class='line-break'> </span>headstone at an expense of $1<sup>50</sup>/100. Where parties are not<span class='line-break'> </span>known the Trustees require payment in advance.</p>
<p>As soon as the above amount is paid the Treasurer (at<span class='line-break'> </span>16 Pemberton Sq) he will inform this office by telephone<span class='line-break'> </span>and the stone will be set at once.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157446">CB06_0217</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='217'>217</span></p>
<p>May 22 [18]82</p>
<p>Chas H Barnes Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have looked up the matter of the<span class='line-break'> </span>charge for foundation in the Mudd lot 2832 and find<span class='line-break'> </span>the error was in the former charge not the one just rendered.</p>
<p>The foundation charged in  1880 was entered as only 2'-6" x 1'3"<span class='line-break'> </span>and charged $7 - The size was altered on the foremans book<span class='line-break'> </span>to 2'-10" x 1'-4" but the charge was not changed. The size <span class='line-break'> </span>of the foundation just built was 2'-10" x 1'-8"</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157447">
<h3><a name="page-1157447">CB06_0218</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='218'>218</span></p>
<p>May 22nd [18]82</p>
<p>Henry Murray Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In regard to foundation for bowlder at<span class='line-break'> </span>grave of Isaiah Hanscom. If it is a natural field <span class='line-break'> </span>bowlder of which any side is the top I don't think a foundation<span class='line-break'> </span>needed. But if it is a carved marble one that would<span class='line-break'> </span>be hurt if the earth eased and it fell or of which it is<span class='line-break'> </span>desired to keep any part plumb then I think a found<span class='line-break'></span>-ation would be needed.  Please inform me as<span class='line-break'> </span>to the character of the stone and I will decide.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='219'>219</span></p>
<p>May 23<sup>rd</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>Dr. S. Parkman Tuckerman</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your memo of the <span class='line-break'> </span>sizes of the boxes is received and the<span class='line-break'> </span>brick Catacomb will be prepared<span class='line-break'> </span>accordingly - that for Edw<sup>d</sup> Tuckerman<span class='line-break'> </span>in the rear left hand corner, then for<span class='line-break'> </span>Sophia Tuckerman &amp; for Hannah P. Mason</p>
<p>I have sent to M<sup>r</sup> Smith to ascertain<span class='line-break'> </span>what the trouble was in regard to the<span class='line-break'> </span>permits &amp; regret very much that an<span class='line-break'> </span>error in copying those sent him, should<span class='line-break'> </span>have put you to any trouble.</p>
<p>New copies have been sent him which<span class='line-break'> </span>I believe you will find entirely correct<span class='line-break'> </span>and shall hope to have everything<span class='line-break'> </span>completed to your satisfaction next<span class='line-break'> </span>Monday.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157450">CB06_0221</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='221'>221</span></p>
<p>May 23rd [18]82</p>
<p>Edward S. Bowland Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>New York</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In ordering your lot 1265 cared<span class='line-break'> </span>for you requested that it be put in perfect order. I<span class='line-break'> </span>have examined the lot and find it needs returfing.</p>
<p>I would advise you to remove the fence cut over<span class='line-break'> </span>and leave 4 posts at corners, cut the number of lot on one<span class='line-break'> </span>of them and grade and sod throughout. The cost<span class='line-break'> </span>will be $35. with the old material of fence.</p>
<p>If the fence is kept it will cost $52 to paint it<span class='line-break'> </span>and do presodding.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1157451">
<h3><a name="page-1157451">CB06_0222</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='222'>222</span></p>
<p>May 24 [188]2</p>
<p>Edwin H. Sampson Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I think that<span class='line-break'> </span>the hemlock tree on the corner of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Wyman lot next to yours would<span class='line-break'> </span>have to be removed to do much<span class='line-break'> </span>good.</p>
<p>I think I wrote you before that<span class='line-break'> </span>in my opinion the drip from the<span class='line-break'> </span>vines did quite as much harm<span class='line-break'> </span>as the tree, but tho' you wrote me<span class='line-break'> </span>I might trim them considerably. I<span class='line-break'> </span>thought when the vines were out more,<span class='line-break'> </span>it could be better seen how much<span class='line-break'> </span>harm they did.</p>
<p>Perhaps your best way could be<span class='line-break'> </span>to have the gardener go to a lot<span class='line-break'> </span>with you &amp; trim while you were<span class='line-break'> </span>set what would be better removed<span class='line-break'> </span>or if you leave it to us, I<span class='line-break'> </span>will have it attended to<span class='line-break'> </span>as judisciously as possible</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1157454">
<h3><a name="page-1157454">CB06_0225</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='225'>225</span></p>
<p>May 27<sup>th</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>Alex M<sup>c</sup>Donald Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>M<sup>r</sup> Rod<sup>k</sup> Richardson<span class='line-break'> </span>has written me in regard to a foundation<span class='line-break'> </span>which he stated was wrongly built, and<span class='line-break'> </span>I replied that it was built as ordered.<span class='line-break'> </span>He then wrote me that he signed the<span class='line-break'> </span>order in blank^<sup>at your office</sup> and that he did<span class='line-break'> </span>not put on the diagram showing where<span class='line-break'> </span>the foundation was to be built, &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>requested me to setle with you, as<span class='line-break'> </span>the mistake was between us.</p>
<p>I built the foundation exactly where<span class='line-break'> </span>they were ordered and if they are wrong<span class='line-break'> </span>I am ready to move them when I am<span class='line-break'> </span>paid for it.</p>
<p>It will cost $3.<sup>00</sup> to move the foundation<span class='line-break'> </span>and I will have this done whenever you<span class='line-break'> </span>send me an order to do it at your<span class='line-break'> </span>Expense.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1157455">
<h3><a name="page-1157455">CB06_0226</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='226'>226</span></p>
<p>May 27<sup>th</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>Rod<sup>k</sup> Richardson Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Yours of the 26<sup>th</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>rec'd. When your order was rec'd<span class='line-break'> </span>by me, it had on the back the<span class='line-break'> </span>diagram which I copied on to the<span class='line-break'> </span>blank sent you, and if you did not<span class='line-break'> </span>put it there, it must have been done<span class='line-break'> </span>by M<sup>r</sup> M<sup>c</sup>Donald or his assistants<span class='line-break'> </span>I have notified him I was ready to<span class='line-break'> </span>move the foundation at his expense.</p>
<p>I am ready, always to promptly<span class='line-break'> </span>correct all my sure mistakes, but <span class='line-break'> </span>I think you should not hold me<span class='line-break'> </span>responsible for his.<span class='line-break'> </span>(over)</p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt</p>
<p>Your postal to me some weeks<span class='line-break'> </span>ago only states that you proposed<span class='line-break'> </span>to have M<sup>r </sup>M<sup>c</sup>Donald erect some<span class='line-break'> </span>headstone (you do not say where or<span class='line-break'> </span>at whose graves) and repair the<span class='line-break'> </span>monument.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157456">
<h3><a name="page-1157456">CB06_0227</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='227'>227</span></p>
<p>May 31<sup>st</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>Mrs Andrew Robeson</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>I have carefully ex<span class='line-break'></span>amined your lot with reference to<span class='line-break'> </span>the change of grade which you spoke<span class='line-break'> </span>to me about, and while I would<span class='line-break'> </span>much prefer to have no change<span class='line-break'> </span>made, still if you find the present<span class='line-break'> </span>grade so unsatisfactory to you, and<span class='line-break'> </span>are disposed to go to so large an<span class='line-break'> </span>expense, it might perhaps be arranged.</p>
<p>I doubt if the general appearance would<span class='line-break'> </span>be improved by the change, and it<span class='line-break'> </span>does not seem to me that any improve<span class='line-break'></span>ment which you would devise from it,<span class='line-break'> </span>would warrant so large an expense.</p>
<p>The reason of the great expense about<span class='line-break'> </span>the change is that the embankment<span class='line-break'> </span>would have to be formed again<span class='line-break'> </span>from the bottom in order to have<span class='line-break'> </span>the grade of the bank regular</p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1157459">
<h3><a name="page-1157459">CB06_0230</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='230'>230</span></p>
<p>May 31<sup>st</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>Miss Kate L. Fowle</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>With reference<span class='line-break'> </span>to your lot, I think that you could<span class='line-break'> </span>probably dispose of it during the<span class='line-break'> </span>summer and if you will let me<span class='line-break'> </span>know what you would sell it<span class='line-break'> </span>for I will see what I can do.</p>
<p>I do not know what the cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>moving the monument &amp; remains from<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston would be, probably not a<span class='line-break'> </span>great dea. To take them from here<span class='line-break'> </span>and deliver at the depot of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston &amp; Main R.R. in Boston would<span class='line-break'> </span>cost about $15.<sup>00</sup></p>
<p>The fence would only ask as old<span class='line-break'> </span>since having been a long time without<span class='line-break'> </span>care.</p>
<p>I think I could get you $300 for the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot now.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>Lot N<sup>o</sup> 1532</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157471">CB06_0242</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='242'>242</span></p>
<p>June 5<sup>th</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>Charles Merriam Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of the<span class='line-break'> </span>4<sup>th</sup> inst is received &amp; will have careful<span class='line-break'> </span>attention.</p>
<p>The lot has not suffered from<span class='line-break'> </span>neglect although I know the ivies<span class='line-break'> </span>are not as you would like to see them.<span class='line-break'> </span>I personaly examined the lot with<span class='line-break'> </span>the gardener several weeks ago and<span class='line-break'> </span>found several of the Japanese ivies<span class='line-break'> </span>dead (these were replaced at the<span class='line-break'> </span>earliest date the season would permit)<span class='line-break'> </span>and the ends of the ivies which run<span class='line-break'> </span>on the trellis were found to be<span class='line-break'> </span>dead (winter killed) in the roots.<span class='line-break'> </span>The [?] very vigorous<span class='line-break'> </span>much larger than any new plants<span class='line-break'> </span>which could be put in.</p>
<p>The gardener believed that by trimming<span class='line-break'> </span>the ivy &amp; letting it start again from<span class='line-break'> </span>the roots the trellis would be more<span class='line-break'> </span>quickly covered than with new<span class='line-break'> </span>plants.</p>
<p>It has not been warm enough<span class='line-break'> </span>to put out madeira vines until<span class='line-break'> </span>now &amp; they would not have borne<span class='line-break'> </span>the cold nights had they been<span class='line-break'> </span>put out. During the last two weeks<span class='line-break'> </span>we have lost many plants which<span class='line-break'> </span>are much more hardy than the vine<span class='line-break'> </span>and no [lesson?] has been so [backed?] <span class='line-break'> </span>as the present during my connection<span class='line-break'> </span>here.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1157479">CB06_0250</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='250'>250</span></p>
<p>June 27<sup>th</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>Brice S. Evans Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your note received ordering<span class='line-break'> </span>grass cut on the late Mr C W Cumming's lot</p>
<p>The Trustees have directed me to do no work<span class='line-break'> </span>on lots where there are unpaid bills.<span class='line-break'> </span>There is a bill of $3.50 due on this lot<span class='line-break'> </span>since 1873. If you will see our Treasurer<span class='line-break'> </span>(16 Pemberton Sqr) and arrange the matter the<span class='line-break'> </span>work will be gone on with at once.</p>
<p>Also please say if you desire the grass<span class='line-break'> </span>cut only once or during the season.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
<p>[letter voided]</p>
<p>June 26th [188]2</p>
<p>Brice S Evans Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Yours of 24th received.</p>
<p>I take it you wish the grass on the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot of Mr Chas. W. Cummings cut during<span class='line-break'> </span><u>the season</u> and have so ordered the work.<span class='line-break'> </span>If you desire it only once cut please<span class='line-break'> </span>inform me.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J C S<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>June 27th [188]2</p>
<p>R.A. Ballow Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your order for work on<span class='line-break'> </span>lot #3837 is received. I am directed<span class='line-break'> </span>by vote of the Trustees to do no work<span class='line-break'> </span>on lots where there are unpaid bills.<span class='line-break'> </span>There has a [?] been due on Lot<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] since 1874 and this will have to<span class='line-break'> </span>be paid or the work now ordered<span class='line-break'> </span>paid in advance. I enclose a<span class='line-break'> </span>bill for the work to be done in case<span class='line-break'> </span>you elect to take the latter course.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<p>July 5th [188]2</p>

<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have examined lot<span class='line-break'> </span>#86 - Blood. To remove fence, grade and<span class='line-break'> </span>sod will cost $40 and old material.<span class='line-break'> </span>If fence remains the grading &amp; sodding<span class='line-break'> </span>will cost $50.</p>
<p>The fence will bring very little but if<span class='line-break'> </span>the parties are not inclined to do<span class='line-break'> </span>anything further, to induce them to<span class='line-break'> </span>remove it, will do that, cutting over the<span class='line-break'> </span>4 corner posts, cutting number etc. for<span class='line-break'> </span>the old material.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S. Supt</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157485">CB06_0256</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='256'>256</span></p>
<p>July 6<sup>th</sup> [188]2.</p>
<p>Messrs D.L. Kent &amp; Co.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In answer to yours<span class='line-break'> </span>of the 16<sup>th</sup> ult<sup>o.</sup>I would say that<span class='line-break'> </span>I wrote you last Feby. that C.H.<span class='line-break'> </span>Allcote was the only person among<span class='line-break'> </span>the five names for whom you sent<span class='line-break'> </span>headstones, buried here and that<span class='line-break'> </span>his friends declined to have the<span class='line-break'> </span>stone placed on their lot.</p>
<p>I also wrote you that they were<span class='line-break'> </span>here subject to your order &amp; acting<span class='line-break'> </span>at your risk &amp; as they are in our way<span class='line-break'> </span>I should be glad to have them<span class='line-break'> </span>removed.</p>
<p>By communicating with there<span class='line-break'> </span>in charge of Cambridge City Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>is the Catholic Cemetery, it is possible<span class='line-break'> </span>you may find where they belong.<span class='line-break'> </span>but if you can't get information<span class='line-break'> </span>from them, I don't know where it<span class='line-break'> </span>is to be found.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1157486">CB06_0257</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='257'>257</span></p>
<p>July 10th [188]2</p>
<p>Geo E Smith Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In regard to your inquiries<span class='line-break'> </span>as to headstones in the Pearl lot. The<span class='line-break'> </span>headstones are not out of plumb they<span class='line-break'> </span>only seem so because of the grade<span class='line-break'> </span>of the lot.  The matter of the curbing<span class='line-break'> </span>on opposite side of the path has been<span class='line-break'> </span>brought to the attention of the Trustees.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
<p>July 10 [188]2</p>
<p>Mrs F.H. Stimpson</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>The grass on<span class='line-break'> </span>your lot appears to be in very fair<span class='line-break'> </span>condition and I think the "lumps &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>rough places" mentioned must have<span class='line-break'> </span>disappeared almost entirely. The few<span class='line-break'> </span>inequalities now on the lot might<span class='line-break'> </span>be removed next September, by seeding<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot and filling these depressions<span class='line-break'> </span>with loan, which would not be an<span class='line-break'> </span>expensive matter.</p>
<p>I find that the diagram of interments<span class='line-break'> </span>has already been placed on the register.<span class='line-break'> </span>You will receive the perpetual care estimate<span class='line-break'> </span>soon.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering <span class='line-break'> </span>Supt </p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1157487">
<h3><a name="page-1157487">CB06_0258</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='258'>258</span></p>
<p>July 11th [188]2</p>
<p>E.H Higgins Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Groton Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your note is received. I<span class='line-break'> </span>have examined your lot and think you will<span class='line-break'> </span>do well to remove the fence. The old mat<span class='line-break'></span>-erial of it will pay for removal, cutting<span class='line-break'> </span>over 4 posts for corners that is having<span class='line-break'> </span>a stonecutter cut off enough to remove the<span class='line-break'> </span>ends of iron rods - cut the number<span class='line-break'> </span>of lot one one of the posts - and filling up<span class='line-break'> </span>and sodding over the other posts holes.</p>
<p>There is no use of top dressing or<span class='line-break'> </span>caring for the lot unless it is returfed.<span class='line-break'> </span>There is nothing there now but weeds</p>
<p>To regrade and resod will cost $40.<span class='line-break'> </span>This will leave the lot all in good order.</p>
<p>If you leave the fence there it<span class='line-break'> </span>will cost $50 to put the lot in good order.</p>
<p>In regard to the perpetual care of the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot I will wait until I hear from you as to<span class='line-break'> </span>what you propose doing and I will then<span class='line-break'> </span>be better able to make an estimate.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1157489">
<h3><a name="page-1157489">CB06_0260</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='260'>260</span></p>
<p>July 12 [188]2</p>
<p>Miss Helen M. Parsons<span class='line-break'> </span>Roxbury</p>
<p>Madam</p>
<p>Your note received. The<span class='line-break'> </span>charge for planting myrtle is $7. for<span class='line-break'> </span>each full size grave. The laurel<span class='line-break'> </span>in the border was not done very well. The<span class='line-break'> </span>trouble is not with the shrub however but<span class='line-break'> </span>because there is too much shade and<span class='line-break'> </span>any other shrub put in its place would<span class='line-break'> </span>act in the same way. Still I would<span class='line-break'> </span>not advise cutting any of the trees as<span class='line-break'> </span>that would be much more of a sacrifice<span class='line-break'> </span>than there would be gain in having a shrub<span class='line-break'> </span>in the border.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
<p>July 12th [188]2</p>
<p>Mrs Joanna P Morse<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>I have examined into<span class='line-break'> </span>the matter of your order for care of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Emmons lot #852 and find that<span class='line-break'> </span>on May 12th [18]80 you gave a signed order<span class='line-break'> </span>to the gardener which reads "Care of lot until<span class='line-break'> </span>counter manded." And in accordance with<span class='line-break'> </span>it the lot was cared for 1880 &amp; 81 as attested<span class='line-break'> </span>by the returns from the foreman and<span class='line-break'> </span>workman. I see no reason why the bill<span class='line-break'> </span>should not be paid. The order is on file at<span class='line-break'> </span>this office &amp; can be seen by you at anytime.</p>
<p>The foreman reports that no grave enclosure has been<span class='line-break'> </span>removed from the lot to his knowledge.</p>
<p>very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1157492">
<h3><a name="page-1157492">CB06_0263</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='263'>263</span></p>
<p>July 14th [188]2</p>
<p>Messrs Leighton &amp; Liberty<span class='line-break'> </span>Deering Me</p>
<p>Gentlemen</p>
<p>Your note received.<span class='line-break'> </span>The foundation can be built at about<span class='line-break'> </span>48 hours notice. Where parties are<span class='line-break'> </span>unknown to us our rule is cash in advance.<span class='line-break'> </span>You give three sizes for this foundation so<span class='line-break'> </span>I am not sure which is the width.<span class='line-break'> </span>If the size is 2'-8" x 1'-2" the charge<span class='line-break'> </span>will be $7.00. If 2'-8" x 1'-0" it will be<span class='line-break'> </span>$5.60. If inconvenient for you to remit<span class='line-break'> </span>you had better order through Mrs. Furbush.</p>
<p>The lot is 4381 Marigold Pa. I mentions this<span class='line-break'> </span>as you said Magnolia and there is a chance<span class='line-break'> </span>for mistake</p>
<p>Very respectfully <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1157493">
<h3><a name="page-1157493">CB06_0264</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='264'>264</span></p>
<p>July 15th [188]2</p>
<p>Alex<sup>r</sup> M<sup>c</sup>Donald Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The enclosed letter was<span class='line-break'> </span>sent to me from the Boston office. The sign<span class='line-break'></span>-ature of Mrs Tudor will be needed before a<span class='line-break'> </span>permit can be issued.</p>
<p>respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157494">CB06_0265</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='265'>265</span></p>
<p>July 14th [188]2</p>
<p>Mrs L.B. Ryder<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>In regard to the<span class='line-break'> </span>mistake in opening grave this after<span class='line-break'></span>-noon. Your letter ordered it dug "<u>to the<span class='line-break'> </span>right of the grave of Cora towards the <span class='line-break'> </span>gate</u>". Whether you referred to the gate<span class='line-break'> </span>of the lot or the gate of the Cemetery that<span class='line-break'> </span>would not describe the location where<span class='line-break'> </span>grave now is.  Last night I<span class='line-break'> </span>telephoned Mr Litchfield that the descrip<span class='line-break'></span>-tion was not clear and he called and<span class='line-break'> </span>agreed with me that as near as<span class='line-break'> </span>could be judged by your letter the location<span class='line-break'> </span>was where the first grave was opened.</p>
<p>It was agreed however to prevent mistakes<span class='line-break'> </span>that no work should be done until<span class='line-break'> </span>10 a.m today, that I claim gave ample<span class='line-break'> </span>time to communicate with you or some<span class='line-break'> </span>member of your family and have the<span class='line-break'> </span>matter put right. I held the men in<span class='line-break'> </span>attendance waiting for other instructions. I<span class='line-break'> </span>do not desire to render a bill for that and<span class='line-break'> </span>the extra work but think it just to point<span class='line-break'> </span>out to you that the mistake does not<span class='line-break'> </span>lie with any servant of this Corporation.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup't</p>
</div>

<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='280'>280</span></p>
<p>Sept 8<sup>th</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>(Lot 3380)<span class='line-break'> </span>Mrs Anna M Ruggle<span class='line-break'> </span>[Westfield?]<span class='line-break'> </span>N.Y.</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>I have seen the lot and have<span class='line-break'> </span>asked the gardener to give it as<span class='line-break'> </span>much water as possible &amp; this I<span class='line-break'> </span>think is the cause of the neglected<span class='line-break'> </span>appearance.</p>
<p>In regard to the myrtle, I find<span class='line-break'> </span>that three of the graves are some<span class='line-break'></span>what sunken, and that the others<span class='line-break'> </span>need a little repairing. To put<span class='line-break'> </span>the whole in order would cost $7<sup>50</sup></p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157510">
<h3><a name="page-1157510">CB06_0281</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='281'>281</span></p>
<p>Sept 11 [188]2.</p>
<p>H.A. Lamb Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In answer to your<span class='line-break'> </span>favor of the 9<sup>th</sup>, I will say that<span class='line-break'> </span>as the circumstances seem somewhat<span class='line-break'> </span>exceptional, I will try to arrange<span class='line-break'> </span>the payment to meet your views tho'<span class='line-break'> </span>it is usually made according to<span class='line-break'> </span>the terms of the certificate sent<span class='line-break'> </span>you.</p>
<p>As to the size of the lot, I do not<span class='line-break'> </span>remember that any definite size<span class='line-break'> </span>was agreed on. I should have to<span class='line-break'> </span>ask you more for a larger lot<span class='line-break'> </span>and as it is only wanted for<span class='line-break'> </span>one burial, would it make any<span class='line-break'> </span>difference? I do not see that<span class='line-break'> </span>much more land could be sold<span class='line-break'> </span>at all, as an addition to this lot,<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; certainly there would seem to be<span class='line-break'> </span>no chance of selling any to<span class='line-break'> </span>any one else.</p>
<p>Ys very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157511">
<h3><a name="page-1157511">CB06_0282</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='282'>282</span></p>
<p>Sept 15<sup>th</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>George T. Angell Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In answer to<span class='line-break'> </span>your note, I would say that no<span class='line-break'> </span>stonework can be placed around<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot you selected and that<span class='line-break'> </span>but few enclosures of any kind are<span class='line-break'> </span>now erected.</p>
<p>At no quorum of Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>present at the meeting called for<span class='line-break'> </span>Wednesday, no action of any kind<span class='line-break'> </span>was taken in regard to a fountain<span class='line-break'> </span>or water, tho' I mentioned the subject<span class='line-break'> </span>to several of the gentlemen present.</p>
<p>I have ascertained that the only way<span class='line-break'> </span>in which good water can be procured<span class='line-break'> </span>would be to lay a pipe from close by<span class='line-break'> </span>our front gate to your lot, which<span class='line-break'> </span>would cost $500. and that the<span class='line-break'> </span>water could be obtained from the<span class='line-break'> </span>City for 2 cents per 100 gallons.</p>
<p>You were going as I understood it<span class='line-break'> </span>to send a written petition in regard<span class='line-break'> </span>to the name "Band of Mercy" after con<span class='line-break'></span>sidering the matter, as I take you that<span class='line-break'> </span>the Trustees must act on any<span class='line-break'> </span>changes of name.</p>
<p>There will probably be a meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>called before long, &amp; perhaps it would<span class='line-break'> </span>be well to send me a written<span class='line-break'> </span>statement to lay before the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>of your exact wishes in regard<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Fountain, water supply<span class='line-break'> </span>name of path &amp;c, which would<span class='line-break'> </span>be more definite than anything</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157512">
<h3><a name="page-1157512">CB06_0283</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='283'>283</span></p>
<p>I can now tell them.</p>
<p>No change has been made in<span class='line-break'> </span>Central Square except by closing up<span class='line-break'> </span>a small path between the lot you<span class='line-break'> </span>selected &amp; a smaller one on the East side<span class='line-break'> </span>(the opposite sides from the pump.) The<span class='line-break'> </span>name Central Sq. has I believe<span class='line-break'> </span>always applied to the path on<span class='line-break'> </span>which the pump stands.</p>
<p>I think a half lot can, perhaps, be<span class='line-break'> </span>arranged for your friend W<sup>m</sup> Noyes<span class='line-break'> </span>next to yours, the cost of which<span class='line-break'> </span>would be $400.</p>
<p>Yrs Truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157513">
<h3><a name="page-1157513">CB06_0284</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='284'>284</span></p>
<p>Sept 15<sup>th</sup> [188]2</p>
<p>Joseph B. Glover Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I send you a plan<span class='line-break'> </span>of the arrangement of catacombs for<span class='line-break'> </span>your lot which leaves few spares in<span class='line-break'> </span>center of the lot than I had supposed.</p>
<p>The best suggestion I can make if<span class='line-break'> </span>all of the catacombs are wanted is<span class='line-break'> </span>that the catacomb which I have marked<span class='line-break'> </span>with a cross should be moved to one<span class='line-break'> </span>of the two positions which I have in<span class='line-break'></span>dicated in the plan by xx (i.e. either<span class='line-break'> </span>the front or back right hand portion of<span class='line-break'> </span>lot.) which will leave room for a<span class='line-break'> </span>monument, if not too large in the center<span class='line-break'> </span>of the lot, but toward the front so as<span class='line-break'> </span>not to lap over the vacant catacomb<span class='line-break'> </span>next to that one in which the burial<span class='line-break'> </span>of Jane Glover was made.</p>
<p>I think the base of the monuments if<span class='line-break'> </span>square should not exceed 3 or 4 ft.<span class='line-break'> </span>If sq sarcophagus should be erected<span class='line-break'> </span>it could be 6 or 7 ft x 3'-4'.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157514">
<h3><a name="page-1157514">CB06_0285</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='285'>285</span></p>
<p>Sept 15<sup>th</sup> [188]2.</p>
<p>Joseph R. Glover Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I send you a plan<span class='line-break'> </span>of the arrangement of catacombs in<span class='line-break'> </span>your lot which leaves less space in the<span class='line-break'> </span>center of the lot than I had supposed.</p>
<p>The best suggestion I can make, if<span class='line-break'> </span>all of the catacombs are wanted, is<span class='line-break'> </span>that the catacomb which I have marked<span class='line-break'> </span>with a cross should be moved to one<span class='line-break'> </span>of the two positions which I have in<span class='line-break'></span>dicated on the plan by xx, (i.e either<span class='line-break'> </span>the front or back right hand portion of<span class='line-break'> </span>lot.) which will leave room for a<span class='line-break'> </span>monument, if not too large in the center<span class='line-break'> </span>of the lot, but toward the front, so as<span class='line-break'> </span>not to lap over the vacant catacomb<span class='line-break'> </span>next to the one in which the burial<span class='line-break'> </span>of Jane Glover was made.</p>
<p>I think the base of the monument if<span class='line-break'> </span>square should not exceed 3 or 4 ft sq.<span class='line-break'> </span>If a sarcophagus should be erected<span class='line-break'> </span>it could be 6 or 7 ft x 3' or 4'.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<p>Jacob Sleeper Esq</p>

<p>The price for the<span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care of your lot has been<span class='line-break'> </span>reconsidered, as you requested, but<span class='line-break'> </span>it does not appear that any reduc<span class='line-break'></span>tion should be made in the price<span class='line-break'> </span>named to you ($575 including the<span class='line-break'> </span>cleaning but not the renewal of the<span class='line-break'> </span>marble) unless you will dispense with<span class='line-break'> </span>the flowers in front, when the unit<span class='line-break'> </span>would be reduced to $500.</p>

<p>Yrs respectfully <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157524">CB06_0295</a></h3>

<p>Oct. 9<sup>th</sup> [188]2.</p>
<p>T.M. Merriman Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>West Dedham</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Can you<span class='line-break'> </span>inform me whether in placing<span class='line-break'> </span>the bodies now in the grave which<span class='line-break'> </span>you own (&amp; in which you have pe<span class='line-break'></span>titioned the Trustee to allow a<span class='line-break'> </span>third interment,) the matter of<span class='line-break'> </span>making a third interment was<span class='line-break'> </span>provided for and the bodies placed<span class='line-break'> </span>at an extra depth so as to leave<span class='line-break'> </span>room for a burial above without<span class='line-break'> </span>coming within three feet of the<span class='line-break'> </span>surface</p>
<p>If this was not done, should you<span class='line-break'> </span>wish to have the bodies now then<span class='line-break'> </span>lowered so that it could be done<span class='line-break'> </span>at your expense &amp; provided that the<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustee, as soon as the was done<span class='line-break'> </span>would grant you the privilege of<span class='line-break'> </span>making the three interment?</p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157528">CB06_0299</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='299'>299</span></p>
<p>Oct 18th [188]2.</p>
<p>Mrs Charles A. Prince</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>In answer to your<span class='line-break'> </span>note to M<sup>r</sup> Collins with reference<span class='line-break'> </span>to the condition of lot #1158 (Prince)<span class='line-break'> </span>I would say that no order has been<span class='line-break'> </span>given for care and repair on this<span class='line-break'> </span>lot for more than four or five years.</p>
<p>The grass can be kept cut by<span class='line-break'> </span>your sending an annual or a permanent<span class='line-break'> </span>order in writing to that effect, and<span class='line-break'> </span>such other repairs as may be desired<span class='line-break'> </span>from time to time will be made when<span class='line-break'> </span>ordered; or you can make a permanent<span class='line-break'> </span>arrangement for care and repair according<span class='line-break'> </span>to the circular enclosed.</p>
<p>In regard to the Rufus Choate lot<span class='line-break'> </span>the orders received were for the cutting<span class='line-break'> </span>of the grass, the trimming of the vines &amp; the<span class='line-break'> </span>enriching of the sod (the latter to be done<span class='line-break'> </span>this fall)</p>
<p>This is the first year the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>has cared for the lot and I do not<span class='line-break'> </span>know how well it may have looked<span class='line-break'> </span>in past years, but it is in much<span class='line-break'> </span>better order than when taken in the<span class='line-break'> </span>spring.</p>
<p>There are four trees in the lot, besides<span class='line-break'> </span>several near, which give too much<span class='line-break'> </span>shade for good grass.</p>
<p>The removal of all or a part of the<span class='line-break'> </span>trees in the lot &amp; the painting of the<span class='line-break'> </span>fence would improve the lot as<span class='line-break'> </span>would resodding, but it is of no use to<span class='line-break'> </span>go to the expense of resodding with so much shade.<span class='line-break'> </span>Any instructions you may send will be promptly attended to</p>
<p>Very truly <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1157542">CB06_0313</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='313'>313</span></p>
<p>Nov 8th [188]2</p>
<p>Frank A Homer Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your note in regard<span class='line-break'> </span>to the charge for myrtle is received.</p>
<p>From your order filed in this office I<span class='line-break'> </span>find you gave directions to prepare<span class='line-break'> </span>a grave for myrtle at our usual charge<span class='line-break'> </span>of $3. You gave a further order<span class='line-break'> </span>to put more myrtle on the grave of<span class='line-break'> </span>Mrs Homer to be charged extra.</p>
<p>The gardener states that all the myrtle<span class='line-break'> </span>was planted on the grave prepared<span class='line-break'> </span>and that you sent only sufficient for<span class='line-break'> </span>that. No myrtle was put on the<span class='line-break'> </span>other grave and no charge made.</p>
<p>The charge of $3 is perfectly legitimate<span class='line-break'> </span>that being our established price and<span class='line-break'> </span>is in accordance with your written<span class='line-break'> </span>order.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157551">CB06_0322</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='322'>322</span></p>
<p>Dec. 12<sup>th</sup> [188]2.</p>
<p>C.B. Caufield Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In ansewr to your favor as<span class='line-break'> </span>of the 11<sup>th</sup> inst. I would say that the distance<span class='line-break'> </span>from the present back line of the inner<span class='line-break'> </span>curbing, to the headstones is 11 to 12 inches &amp; that<span class='line-break'> </span>the width of the bases of the headstones is 17 inches<span class='line-break'> </span>making from lot line to the front of the bases<span class='line-break'> </span>of headstones 2'-4" or 5". Ordinarily, the proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>of lots here own only the land enclosed in<span class='line-break'> </span>the <u>inner</u> enclosure: with a right of passage<span class='line-break'> </span>from the Avenue, only, but in this case the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot was originally laid out differently,<span class='line-break'> </span>and the shape was altered when the<span class='line-break'> </span>present curbing was put up. M<sup>r</sup> Fiske's<span class='line-break'> </span>deed calls for five hundred feet, but<span class='line-break'> </span>there is at present enclosed about 418 ft.<span class='line-break'> </span>leaving 82 ft not included in the inner<span class='line-break'> </span>enclosure which belongs to him.</p>
<p>If he prefers to place the monument<span class='line-break'> </span>at the head of the graves, as the headstones<span class='line-break'> </span>now stand, I think it might be arranged<span class='line-break'> </span>as that he could occupy land back of<span class='line-break'> </span>his present line &amp; then make up the 82 ft<span class='line-break'> </span>which belong to him, tho' it does not seem<span class='line-break'> </span>as if he could go back as much as 3'-4"<span class='line-break'> </span>which would be needed to make up the<span class='line-break'> </span>width of the foundation in addition to the land<span class='line-break'> </span>now between the line &amp; the front of the headstone<span class='line-break'> </span>bases, without interfering with the next lots,<span class='line-break'> </span>but he might go back enough to answer the<span class='line-break'> </span>purpose. If the owner of the next lot should<span class='line-break'> </span>ever put up a stone line, which by his deed<span class='line-break'> </span>he has the right to do, the monument would,<span class='line-break'> </span>if seems to me, come very near to it. &amp; look too<span class='line-break'> </span>crowded, perhaps.</p>
<p>Yrs truly <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<p>The bill of $6<sup>50</sup> which you paid for<span class='line-break'> </span>lot #2147 on Oct 30<sup>th</sup> paid for the care of<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot which consists in keeping the grass<span class='line-break'> </span>cut &amp; the lot raked off &amp; clean, and for<span class='line-break'> </span>top dressing with manure.</p>
<p>In making any arrangement for the per<span class='line-break'></span>petual care of the lot, it would be<span class='line-break'> </span>better to arrange if possible for the care<span class='line-break'> </span>of the three lots in the enclosure. This<span class='line-break'> </span>would cost including the painting of<span class='line-break'> </span>the fence &amp; the cleaning of the headstones<span class='line-break'> </span>$1050.00 or if the renewal of the headstones<span class='line-break'> </span>is included the cost would be $250<span class='line-break'> </span>additional.</p>
<p>If the fence were removed the expense<span class='line-break'> </span>of perpetual care would be one hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>and fifty dollars less.</p>
<p>The cost of perpetual care of your lot<span class='line-break'> </span>#2147 alone, would be including the<span class='line-break'> </span>cleaning of the headstones, and the painting<span class='line-break'> </span>of the fences (for as long as the fence on the<span class='line-break'> </span>adjoining lots is kept in order) $450<span class='line-break'> </span>and including the renewal of the headstones<span class='line-break'> </span>$150 additional. If the fence were<span class='line-break'> </span>first removed either estimate would<span class='line-break'> </span>be $75 dollars less.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<div id="page-1157554">
<h3><a name="page-1157554">CB06_0325</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='325'>325</span></p>
<p>Dec 21<sup>st</sup> [188]2.</p>
<p>To the Treas<sup>r</sup>.</p>
<p>The custom has been under<span class='line-break'> </span>the restriction which all in all the<span class='line-break'> </span>deeds now given out reserving to the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corp<sup>n</sup> the right to do all work, to<span class='line-break'> </span>permit headstones to be placed<span class='line-break'> </span>on foundations by parties not in the<span class='line-break'> </span>employ of the Corporation, and to<span class='line-break'> </span>permit them in certain cases to erect<span class='line-break'> </span>monuments where they were known<span class='line-break'> </span>to be careful &amp; responsible people.</p>
<p>While they are not likely to do much<span class='line-break'> </span>damage in setting headstones, they<span class='line-break'> </span>may do much in setting monuments<span class='line-break'> </span>which are heavy &amp; I think the best way<span class='line-break'> </span>is to claim our right to set them whenever<span class='line-break'> </span>they are large enough to do damage. For<span class='line-break'> </span>persons who are known to be unusually<span class='line-break'> </span>careful an [exception?] be made<span class='line-break'> </span>when desirable.</p>
<p>Our practice has been to apply the<span class='line-break'> </span>rule to all lots under p.c. which<span class='line-break'> </span><u>includes</u> of course all which are<span class='line-break'> </span>under the present form of deed.</p>
<p>I think under the restrictions in<span class='line-break'> </span>the deeds, all steps, posts or enclosures<span class='line-break'> </span>should be set by our own employees.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
<p>P.S<span class='line-break'> </span>In this case I see no objection to<span class='line-break'> </span>B &amp; T. setting the monument. You can<span class='line-break'> </span>tell them it is on level ground.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W.L</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

The <span class='line-break'> </span>headstone you have erected exceeds<span class='line-break'> </span>that height several inches. <p>I am sorry there<span class='line-break'> </span>has been a mistake in regard to<span class='line-break'> </span>mounding the graves in your lot.</p>

<p>The best way to arrange the curbing<span class='line-break'> </span>will be to move the present back<span class='line-break'> </span>corners over to form the new<span class='line-break'> </span>corners on the path side, and then<span class='line-break'> </span>to put in 25 ft of new stone on<span class='line-break'> </span>each side. The present back will<span class='line-break'> </span>answer, when shortened, for the<span class='line-break'> </span>pieces on each side of the entrance<span class='line-break'> </span>running to the corners, if you propose<span class='line-break'> </span>to have a secure entrance, or if<span class='line-break'> </span>not will form the new line<span class='line-break'> </span>parallel with the path.</p>

<p>When you have made arrange<span class='line-break'></span>ments with the parties who are to<span class='line-break'> </span>do this work if they will call or<span class='line-break'> </span>write to the office, should be glad<span class='line-break'> </span>to see their plan that the dimensions<span class='line-break'> </span>of the new lot may be correct, and<span class='line-break'> </span>if you arrange for the delivery on the<span class='line-break'> </span>avenue of the new stone, I can have<span class='line-break'> </span>the balance done here for you.</p>

<p>Miss S Winslow<span class='line-break'> </span>Worcester Mass.</p>
<p>Madam</p>
<p>Your note is received.<span class='line-break'> </span>The plants were charged at our<span class='line-break'> </span>usual rate of $1.50 per dozen. We set<span class='line-break'> </span>out the plants replace them if they<span class='line-break'> </span>die care for and water them during<span class='line-break'> </span>the season and have therefore to<span class='line-break'> </span>make a higher charge than if <span class='line-break'> </span>our responsibility ended when we hand<span class='line-break'></span>ed you the plants at our greenhouse</p>
<p>I do not know of any florist in this<span class='line-break'> </span>neighbourhood who will set out plants<span class='line-break'> </span>and care for them at a lower<span class='line-break'> </span>charge.</p>
<p>I think $1.50 is a reasonable<span class='line-break'> </span>charge for transplanting the rose<span class='line-break'> </span>etc.  I find by the gardeners ticket<span class='line-break'> </span>that there was used <sup>3</sup>/4 loads loam<span class='line-break'> </span>1 <sup>1</sup>/2 barrows manure and <sup>1</sup>/2 day<span class='line-break'> </span>labor.</p>
<p>I find also that no charge has been<span class='line-break'> </span>made for storing the palm in<span class='line-break'> </span>our greenhouse the usual price<span class='line-break'> </span>for that is $1.50</p>

<div id="page-1157571">
<h3><a name="page-1157571">CB06_0342</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='342'>342</span></p>
<p>Feby 23<sup>rd</sup> [188]3</p>
<p>F.W. Todd Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your letter of Feby 8<sup>th</sup> with<span class='line-break'> </span>plan of the tomb you propose to<span class='line-break'> </span>erect is rec'd and has been submitted<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Committee on Lots, who approve it<span class='line-break'> </span>providing that the whole is built in<span class='line-break'> </span>a thorough &amp; substantial manner, the <span class='line-break'> </span>walls &amp;c not shown on plan to be<span class='line-break'> </span>of material &amp; dimensions satisfactory to<span class='line-break'> </span>the Corporation, that the division walls<span class='line-break'> </span>between the catacombs be of brick (laid<span class='line-break'> </span>in cement) not less than 4 inches thick,<span class='line-break'> </span>with no communication whatever or<span class='line-break'> </span>opening between the catacombs. The<span class='line-break'> </span>shelves to be of slate or other stone,<span class='line-break'> </span>with all joints tightly cemented, the cement<span class='line-break'> </span>used to be of good quality, on all the<span class='line-break'> </span>work and to be mixed with not more<span class='line-break'> </span>than two parts of sand.</p>
<p>The distance from the lot line to the<span class='line-break'> </span>avenue is seven 7 ft. as the avenue<span class='line-break'> </span>is now laid out, and the border should<span class='line-break'> </span>not project beyond that line.</p>
<p>I have a large amount of work<span class='line-break'> </span>to be done the coming summer &amp; shall<span class='line-break'> </span>be unable to undertake the work<span class='line-break'> </span>except by the day.</p>
<p>I can have the work well looked<span class='line-break'> </span>after and furnish 4 good men<span class='line-break'> </span>two of whom will be good masons<span class='line-break'> </span>(when the straw &amp; brick work is put up<span class='line-break'> </span>for sixteen dollars $16<sup>00</sup> per day, with no<span class='line-break'> </span>additional charge for derrick when<span class='line-break'> </span>that may be needed.</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1157572">CB06_0343</a></h3>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='343'>343</span></p>
<p>I have not slate enough on hand to<span class='line-break'> </span>build a tomb, and tho' I have some<span class='line-break'> </span>contracted for, it will be sometime be<span class='line-break'></span>fore I can get it, so that I should pre<span class='line-break'></span>fer to have you furnish the slate, as<span class='line-break'> </span>you intend furnishing all other materials.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157573">CB06_0344</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='344'>344</span></p>
<p>Feby 28<sup>th</sup> [188]3</p>
<p>Geo. S. Jones M.D.</p>
<p>After looking over the<span class='line-break'> </span>plan carefully, I can find no spot<span class='line-break'> </span>near the front entrance better suited<span class='line-break'> </span>to the purpose proposed, than the piece<span class='line-break'> </span>next the pine grove on Garden Ave.</p>
<p>This would make a lot 200 ft long<span class='line-break'> </span>and 45 ft wide &amp; would have a<span class='line-break'> </span>(flower) border on each side, and also<span class='line-break'> </span>an avenue on two sides &amp; a path on<span class='line-break'> </span>one side. If this is too large, I will<span class='line-break'> </span>sell you almost any portion, either<span class='line-break'> </span>in the center, or at either end.</p>
<p>The price for ordinary lots here is<span class='line-break'> </span>$1.75 per foot, but in consideration of<span class='line-break'> </span>the unusual size which you want,<span class='line-break'> </span>I will sell subject to the approval of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees 4500 ft or more, at $1.<sup>33 1/3</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per square foot which includes the<span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care of the grass, it being<span class='line-break'> </span>also understood that no enclosure is<span class='line-break'> </span>to be placed about the lot.</p>
<p>A lot could be laid out of such<span class='line-break'> </span>size as desired on the new land<span class='line-break'> </span>near the tower at from $2<sup>.20</sup> to $2.<sup>70</sup> per<span class='line-break'> </span>square foot.</p>
<p>These places strike me as the most<span class='line-break'> </span>desirable for a lot of the size you<span class='line-break'> </span>want.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
