<p><date when='1883-03-28'>March 28<sup>th</sup> [188]3</date></p>
<p>Mrs H.M. Comstock</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>Enclosed please <span class='line-break'> </span>find the certificate of lot which<span class='line-break'> </span>you have selected.</p>
<p>I understand you propose to en<span class='line-break'></span>close the lot with a granite curbing<span class='line-break'> </span>and therefore suppose you would<span class='line-break'> </span>prefer to have the sod laid after<span class='line-break'> </span>the curb is set, as this will save<span class='line-break'> </span>some expense, and the price of<span class='line-break'> </span>the sod is included in the sale.</p>
<p>Since M<sup>r</sup> Gove's lot was purchased<span class='line-break'> </span>a rule has been made which permits<span class='line-break'> </span>no stone borders to be placed along<span class='line-break'> </span>the edges of paths or avenues, so that<span class='line-break'> </span>while the lot itself can be enclosed<span class='line-break'> </span>with granite and steps can be placed<span class='line-break'> </span>in front, the flower borders cannot be<span class='line-break'> </span>enclosed as on M<sup>r</sup> Gove's.</p>
<p>I call your attention to prevent<span class='line-break'> </span>mistake.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>Please ask the parties of whom you<span class='line-break'> </span>order the curbing to call at the office<span class='line-break'> </span>that the grade of the lot and corners<span class='line-break'> </span>may be understood fully.</p>

<p>H.L. Morse Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>42 Summer St.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>The deed for<span class='line-break'> </span>#1291 (*W.F. Horner) conveyed 460 sq feet<span class='line-break'> </span>but I do not find any mention as<span class='line-break'> </span>to how it was located, so that if<span class='line-break'> </span>you desire to move the corner posts<span class='line-break'> </span>forward so that they will be on line<span class='line-break'> </span>with the adjoining lots, or to widen the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot on the sides, I see no objection, except<span class='line-break'> </span>that it would encroach on the path<span class='line-break'> </span>about the lot, and I think the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>would look much better with the<span class='line-break'> </span>fence removed, and the fence can<span class='line-break'> </span>be removed and the posts moved for<span class='line-break'></span>ward, or sideways so as to mark as<span class='line-break'> </span>many feet of land as you own, at<span class='line-break'> </span>no expense to you, if you allow the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation the proceeds of the old fence.</p>
<p>The perpetual care of the lot, after<span class='line-break'> </span>the fence was removed, including the<span class='line-break'> </span>cleaning but not the removal of <span class='line-break'> </span>the headstones would be ($450)<span class='line-break'> </span>four hundred and fifty dollars.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157603">CB06_0374</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-05-01'>May 1<sup>st</sup> [188]3</date></p>
<p>Hon. F.O. Prince</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I enclose sketch showing<span class='line-break'> </span>the best lot I can make out of the<span class='line-break'> </span>three lots on Ivy Path. Owing to the<span class='line-break'> </span>irregularity of the ground it was nec<span class='line-break'></span>essary, in changing them into one lot<span class='line-break'> </span>to make some slight changes in the<span class='line-break'> </span>lines, which now include five hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>square feet, the price being as before $1100.<span class='line-break'> </span>You will see by the plan that there<span class='line-break'> </span>is room for ten brick catacombs.</p>
<p>I can sell you a lot of 300 square<span class='line-break'> </span>ft. on Agave Path in the rear of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Boarne tomb, which is large enough<span class='line-break'> </span>for ten catacombs, five across the<span class='line-break'> </span>back of the lot, and five across the<span class='line-break'> </span>front, leaving a space in the center<span class='line-break'> </span>for a monument or for one or two more<span class='line-break'> </span>burials for $850, or a larger lot<span class='line-break'> </span>on the same path of four hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>square feet with seven burials across<span class='line-break'> </span>the back of lot and seven across the<span class='line-break'> </span>front, with the same space between<span class='line-break'> </span>the burials as in the lot of 300 ft. The<span class='line-break'> </span>price of this lot would be $1100.</p>
<p>If this latter lot should not be large<span class='line-break'> </span>enough, I can arrange to give you<span class='line-break'> </span>more land. The arrangement of a <span class='line-break'> </span>300 ft lot would be like this,<span class='line-break'> </span>and that of a four hundred ft.<span class='line-break'> </span>lot similar to it, but with seven<span class='line-break'> </span>graves across the back instead of<span class='line-break'> </span>five. Please let me know your<span class='line-break'> </span>decision soon as possible.</p>
<p>[diagram: 5 interments above, space here for monument or interments, 5 interments below]</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt</p>
<p>374</p>

<div id="page-1157614">
<h3><a name="page-1157614">CB06_0385</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-05-22'>May 22nd [188]3</date></p>
<p>Mrs J.W. Hatch<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridgeport</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>In reply to your<span class='line-break'> </span>inquiry as to beds in front of your lot<span class='line-break'> </span>I would say that they can be cut<span class='line-break'> </span>provided they do not project<span class='line-break'> </span>beyond the outer edge of the posts.<span class='line-break'> </span>The space between the posts on your<span class='line-break'> </span>and the lot in front is a mutual <span class='line-break'> </span>walk and plants cannot be set<span class='line-break'> </span>on it.</p>
<p>As the Corporation is responsible for<span class='line-break'> </span>the grass its workmen have to<span class='line-break'> </span>cut the beds. If you purchase<span class='line-break'> </span>the plants here the charge ($1.50 per<span class='line-break'> </span>dozen) includes the opening and<span class='line-break'> </span>preparing of beds. If you supply<span class='line-break'> </span>your own plants a small charge will<span class='line-break'> </span>be made for opening the beds.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

The earth gets baked and<span class='line-break'> </span>dry and the myrtle dies. I will wait<span class='line-break'> </span>until I hear from you before going on<span class='line-break'> </span>with the work.</p>

<div id="page-1157627">
<h3><a name="page-1157627">CB06_0398</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-06-02'>June 2<sup>nd</sup> [188]3</date></p>
<p>Moses A. Dow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>There is no mis<span class='line-break'></span>understanding on the part of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation as to what they have<span class='line-break'> </span>assumed to do on lot #4073 &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>I regret very much the disappoint<span class='line-break'></span>ment you have been caused.</p>
<p>It happened in this way; the<span class='line-break'> </span>workmen prepared a number of<span class='line-break'> </span>small spots on perpetual care<span class='line-break'> </span>lots where the grass had been<span class='line-break'> </span>winter killed, for resodding, and<span class='line-break'> </span>in going over them a second time<span class='line-break'> </span>to put on the sod, by mistake sodded<span class='line-break'> </span>over the grave, thinking it a spot<span class='line-break'> </span>they had stripped for repairs, &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>the gardener on going there to put<span class='line-break'> </span>in the plants which he had been<span class='line-break'> </span>directed to do, finding the grave<span class='line-break'> </span>sodded up, delayed doing so<span class='line-break'> </span>until he had inquired again<span class='line-break'> </span>at the office whether the plants<span class='line-break'> </span>were to go or not. The mistake<span class='line-break'> </span>was discovered &amp; rectified before<span class='line-break'> </span>the receipt of your note, although<span class='line-break'> </span>in the press of work just at deco<span class='line-break'></span>ration day it was delayed.</p>
<p>The time when it is safe to put<span class='line-break'> </span>out plants before decoration day, is<span class='line-break'> </span>very short, and hence there is more<span class='line-break'> </span>danger of mistake then than at<span class='line-break'> </span>other times.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
<p>398</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1157628">
<h3><a name="page-1157628">CB06_0399</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-06-04'>June 4th [188]3</date></p>
<p>J.V. Wellington Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In regard to<span class='line-break'> </span>what was said by Mrs Wellington<span class='line-break'> </span>at the gate yesterday I have been<span class='line-break'> </span>at the lot this morning. I find<span class='line-break'> </span>the border does not look very well<span class='line-break'> </span>it was seeded down last year and<span class='line-break'> </span>the grass has not all come up. Knowing<span class='line-break'> </span>that it had been seeded our men did<span class='line-break'> </span>not spade it up -- so that there is too<span class='line-break'> </span>much grass for a flower bed and not<span class='line-break'> </span>enough to make the beds uniform with the<span class='line-break'> </span>other parts. The only remedy I can see<span class='line-break'> </span>is to sod over the borders.</p>
<p>The headstones are toppled and<span class='line-break'> </span>there are sunken spots in the lot.</p>
<p>If the lot was put under perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care and permission given to remove<span class='line-break'> </span>the fence the proceeds would put all these<span class='line-break'> </span>in order except the myrtle - that<span class='line-break'> </span>will have to be replanted again.<span class='line-break'> </span>The cost would be $10 for that part.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
<p>399</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157630">CB06_0401</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-06-04'>June 4th [188]3</date></p>
<p>F.L. Pratt Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157632">CB06_0403</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-06-09'>June 9<sup>th</sup> [188]3</date></p>
<p>Mrs Alice Gilbert<span class='line-break'> </span>Dear Madam</p>
<p>Your lots No. 1279<span class='line-break'> </span>and 1280 on Central lvenue<span class='line-break'> </span>are 24 inches (twenty four) above<span class='line-break'> </span>the avenue, and would therefore<span class='line-break'> </span>require three steps with 8 inches rise<span class='line-break'> </span>or four steps with 6 inches rise, and<span class='line-break'> </span>the lower step should be two or three<span class='line-break'> </span>inches thicker than the others, in<span class='line-break'> </span>order that no hole may show under<span class='line-break'> </span>it.</p>
<p>The distance from the lot line to<span class='line-break'> </span>the Avenue is six feet, so that if<span class='line-break'> </span>there is a flight of steps, whether there<span class='line-break'> </span>are posts placed at the top &amp; bottom<span class='line-break'> </span>of the flight or not, the whole length<span class='line-break'> </span>of the flight measured from the<span class='line-break'> </span>extreme outside to outside would be<span class='line-break'> </span>six (6) feet.</p>
<p>No ^<sup> curb </sup> stones can be placed along<span class='line-break'> </span>the Avenue line on the sides of the<span class='line-break'> </span>steps.</p>
<p>If your stone cutter does not<span class='line-break'> </span>understand this, if he will inquire<span class='line-break'> </span>at, or write to this office, any other<span class='line-break'> </span>information will be furnished.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157644">CB06_0415</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157645">
<h3><a name="page-1157645">CB06_0416</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-06-12'>June 12 [188]3</date></p>
<p>R. P. Gould. Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>Your note in regard to <span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle on Mrs Whites lot #4176 is received.</p>
<p>The myrtle is partly winter killed as has <span class='line-break'> </span>been the myrtle throughout the cemetery <span class='line-break'> </span>and in our greenhouse yard. Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span>White's myrtle was as carefully covered <span class='line-break'> </span>and looked after as any in the grounds.<span class='line-break'> </span>Evergreens, shrubs etc have all suffered <span class='line-break'> </span>during the past winter as you can see in <span class='line-break'> </span>driving about. It will cost $3<span class='line-break'> </span>to make the needed repairs.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
<p><date when='1883-06-12'>June 12 [188]3</date></p>

<p>The openings were<span class='line-break'> </span>made in lot #1731 as you directed.</p>
<p>We found the body of Bryant O Tilden<span class='line-break'> </span>in a brick grave and that of Geo A<span class='line-break'> </span>Houghton in a box. We sounded with<span class='line-break'> </span>a steel rod for the locations of the others<span class='line-break'> </span>these have been entered on our records<span class='line-break'> </span>and herewith you will find a tracing<span class='line-break'> </span>of the plan. <p>In opening the myrtle had to be<span class='line-break'> </span>disturbed it was nearly dead<span class='line-break'> </span>anyway and could not be put back.<span class='line-break'> </span>Do you wish us to leave the graves as they<span class='line-break'> </span>now are or plant new myrtle?</p>
<p>In regard to the addition<span class='line-break'> </span>I find you can get a strip 2'-6" wide<span class='line-break'> </span>(50 sqr ft) on the side next to the Coffin lot<span class='line-break'> </span>#2850. The price including the deed will<span class='line-break'> </span>be $52<sup>00</sup>/100. A similar strip could be<span class='line-break'> </span>sold on the opposite side of the lot.</p>
<p>The work has been begun on<span class='line-break'> </span>lot #571.</p>

<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>In regard to the order <span class='line-break'> </span>left June 26th. The grading and <span class='line-break'> </span>sodding can be much better done <span class='line-break'> </span>if left until early fall. The <span class='line-break'> </span>charge for resodding you will <span class='line-break'> </span>remember was to be $30- and the <span class='line-break'> </span>old material. As the old material <span class='line-break'> </span>(fence) is not to be removed the charge <span class='line-break'> </span>will be $40.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully,<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.   <span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
<p><date when='1883-06-30'>June 30th [188]3</date></p>
<p>Mrs. Eliza Eddy<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Madam,</p>
<p>In answer to your <span class='line-break'> </span>inquiries as to removal etc. You will <span class='line-break'> </span>be allowed $10 for the grave in St. John <span class='line-break'> </span>lot when vacated. The expense <span class='line-break'> </span>of moving the bodies to the new lot includ<span class='line-break'></span>ing a new box will be $13, and for <span class='line-break'> </span>a new foundation $4.40. The stone<span class='line-break'></span>cutter will probably charge you <span class='line-break'> </span>$3 to cut down the headstone.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully,<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>pr J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<p>The lot certainly is not in as<span class='line-break'> </span>good condition as far as the sod<span class='line-break'> </span>is concerned, as I should like to <span class='line-break'> </span>see it in, but is has been steadily <span class='line-break'> </span>improving since early spring and <span class='line-break'> </span>will I trust be satisfactory before<span class='line-break'> </span>long.</p>
<p>In rgard to the Cemetery plants<span class='line-break'> </span>you will remember that no pro<span class='line-break'></span>vision was made for plants in <span class='line-break'> </span>the deposit for perpetual care, and<span class='line-break'> </span>that you paid by special bill for<span class='line-break'> </span>the year they were placed on the <span class='line-break'> </span>lot.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157663">CB06_0434</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-07-06'>July 6<sup>th</sup> [188]3</date></p>
<p>Col. C. W. Folsom</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>It is not proposed at<span class='line-break'> </span>present to lay out and construct the<span class='line-break'> </span>path in the rear of Mrs Mark's Lot, named<span class='line-break'> </span>Dahlia path on the plan, but if she wishes<span class='line-break'> </span>to increase the size of that Lot, land can<span class='line-break'> </span>be sold her then, with the understanding<span class='line-break'> </span>that Dahlia path will not be built at<span class='line-break'> </span>present.</p>
<p>A lot of 20' x 15' or 20' x 20' on Dahlia<span class='line-break'> </span>path would be sold for $850 and $1100<span class='line-break'> </span>respectively, and these prices include<span class='line-break'> </span>the perpetual care of the grass, which<span class='line-break'> </span>is the only way in which any lots are sold.</p>
<p>Even purchases the layer of these Lots<span class='line-break'> </span>should she desire to enclose with her<span class='line-break'> </span>present Lot, it can be done by paying<span class='line-break'> </span>for the land in the rear of the lots at<span class='line-break'> </span>the same rate as for the lot, less the<span class='line-break'> </span>rate already paid for it as passegeway,<span class='line-break'> </span>but it seems to me it would be better<span class='line-break'> </span>to take it as a separate lot, because the<span class='line-break'> </span>grade of Dahlia path will be lower<span class='line-break'> </span>than Garden Ave. so that it will not<span class='line-break'> </span>be feasible to enclose the new lot with<span class='line-break'> </span>a curb on the same grade as the en<span class='line-break'></span>closure of her present lot, and to lower<span class='line-break'> </span>the grade of the present enclosure on<span class='line-break'> </span>the back (which would be necessary to<span class='line-break'> </span>conform to the proposed grade of Dahlia<span class='line-break'> </span>path, would bring the present lot <span class='line-break'> </span>at the back lower than the adjoining<span class='line-break'> </span>ones, and might not be altogether sat<span class='line-break'></span>isfactory. A smaller addition than that</p>
<p>434</p>

<p><date when='1883-07-25'>July 25<sup>th</sup> [188]3</date></p>
<p>C.W. Cotting Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The Peter Harbey Lot<span class='line-break'> </span>(#2868) was placed under perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care at the close of the year 1878<span class='line-break'> </span>by the payment of $600 for the care of<span class='line-break'> </span>the sod, six myrtle graves, plants in<span class='line-break'> </span>the front borders, and care and <u>renewal</u><span class='line-break'> </span>of five headstones (all of which are <span class='line-break'> </span>not yet erected[)].</p>
<p>The iron fence formerly about the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>was removed and the lot put in<span class='line-break'> </span>good order at an expense of some<span class='line-break'> </span>$85<sup>00</sup> just before the contract for<span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care was made.</p>
<p>The lot has been cared for each year<span class='line-break'> </span>since, by cutting grass, weeding seeding<span class='line-break'> </span>watering &amp; top dressing; plants have been<span class='line-break'> </span>set out in the front borders; the marble<span class='line-break'> </span>has twice received special care &amp; cleaning,<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot has been resodded once (in 1880)<span class='line-break'> </span>and the sod repaired at other times &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>the myrtle has been repaired, all at an<span class='line-break'> </span>expense to Dec 31 [18]82 of $95<sup>50</sup>/100.</p>
<p>An examination of all the perpet<span class='line-break'></span>ual care lots was made last week<span class='line-break'> </span>and I find on my memorandum<span class='line-break'> </span>book an order to repair the sod &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>the myrtle; this work is not yet done.</p>
<p>There are four or five trees near enough<span class='line-break'> </span>to the lot to shade it very considerably<span class='line-break'> </span>and the removal of one, on the left<span class='line-break'> </span>hand side of the lot (near the front<span class='line-break'> </span>corner post) as you stand facing the <span class='line-break'> </span>lot, would give the grass more sun</p>

<div id="page-1157687">
<h3><a name="page-1157687">CB06_0458</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>458</p>
<p>Cambridge <date when='1883-08-03'>Aug. 3 [18]83.</date></p>
<p>J.M. Spelman Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Pres<sup>t</sup> &amp;c.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In 1878 Mr. John F. Poor requested<span class='line-break'> </span>the Trustees to exchange his lot #3119 on Rosebay Ave (con<span class='line-break'></span>taining 865 square ft) for two lots on the Stone Farm of the<span class='line-break'> </span>same size, which they voted to do by his paying for the <span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care of the new lots ($865), nothing being allowed <span class='line-break'> </span>for the graite curbing around lot #3119; but this arrangement<span class='line-break'> </span>was not satisfactory to M<sup>r</sup> Poor.</p>
<p>In 1880 he renewed his request, and the matter <span class='line-break'> </span>was referred to the Comm. on Lots with power, but no<span class='line-break'> </span>agreement was arrived at, as to an exchange, and <span class='line-break'> </span>the lot was finally redivided into two lots, #3119 &amp; #4390<span class='line-break'> </span>containing 432 <sup>1</sup>/2 ft each, at M<sup>r</sup> Poor's request, and it was<span class='line-break'> </span>supposed that the matter was finally settled.</p>
<p>M<sup>r</sup> Poor has been at the Cemetery this week and <span class='line-break'> </span>selected the following lots, one of which he proposes to <span class='line-break'> </span>ask the Comm. to exchange for the two lots #3119 &amp; #4390.<span class='line-break'> </span>1<sup>st</sup> lot on Fountain Ave 400 ft. price $1200- (<sup>land</sup>800 + <sup>perpetual care</sup>300  + <sup>sod'g grad'g post &amp;c</sup>100)<span class='line-break'> </span>2<sup>nd</sup> [lot on] Smilax path 400 ft [price] $1080- (700 + 300 + 80)</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157688">
<h3><a name="page-1157688">CB06_0459</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>459</p>
<p>Lots 3119 &amp; 4390 contain 865 ft, are not under perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care, and are enclosed by a granite curbing, in common<span class='line-break'> </span>with Lot #3120 (Stickney)</p>
<p>If the Corporation made the exchange, unless M<sup>r </sup>Stickney<span class='line-break'> </span>or his friends would purchase the Lots #3119 &amp; 4390, as they are<span class='line-break'> </span>large lots, and enclosed in a curbing with another Lot, they<span class='line-break'> </span>could not be sold as readily as if the curbing were removed.</p>
<p>To remove the curbing from the two Poor Lots, and leave<span class='line-break'> </span>the Stickney Lots enclosed, moving the steps now common to<span class='line-break'> </span>both Lots, to the front of the Stickney lot, would probably cost<span class='line-break'> </span>$125, and when this was done the land could be sold<span class='line-break'> </span>in two, or perhaps more readily in four, lots of two hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>feet each, price $450 = (land $250 + perpet. care $150 + grad etc $50),<span class='line-break'> </span>the sale of the four yielding $1000 for land, 6oo for perpetual care <span class='line-break'> </span>and $200 for the grading &amp;c.</p>
<p>The $600 would go into the fund for the care of the four<span class='line-break'> </span>new lots; the $200 would remove the old curbing from lots 3119<span class='line-break'> </span>4390 and reset it around the Stickney lot #3120, (leaving the<span class='line-break'> </span>space occupied by the Poor Lots unenclosed) and provide the<span class='line-break'> </span>necessary corner posts &amp;c to mark the new lots; the $1000 the<span class='line-break'> </span>proceeds of the land alone, would be available therefore toward<span class='line-break'> </span>the payment of the new lot selected, one of which costs $1080<span class='line-break'> </span>and the other $1250.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p>Miss E.B. Pond<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>In regard to the<span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle on the Pond lot 4034 the<span class='line-break'> </span>gard[e]ner reports that there are<span class='line-break'> </span>13 graves that need repairs and<span class='line-break'> </span>that there is only enough myrtle on<span class='line-break'> </span>all of them to make three good graves.</p>

<p>As the work cannot be done until fall<span class='line-break'> </span>perhaps you had better see the gard[e]ner on the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot sometime.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>[J.W. Lovering]</p>

<div id="page-1157705">
<h3><a name="page-1157705">CB06_0476</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>476</p>
<p><date when='1883-08-30'>Aug 30 [188]3</date></p>
<p>Miss Alice C. Mann</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>To paint the fence<span class='line-break'> </span>on lot #1324 will cost ten dollars ($10)<span class='line-break'> </span>and to clean the headstones five dollars ($5)</p>
<p>I should advise the removal of<span class='line-break'> </span>the fence, leaving four of the granite<span class='line-break'> </span>posts on which it rests to mark the<span class='line-break'> </span>corners, which can be recut to look neatly.<span class='line-break'> </span>The proceeds of the fence sold as old iron<span class='line-break'> </span>will pay for the alteration, and the<span class='line-break'> </span>expense of painting every few years will<span class='line-break'> </span>be saved besides the appearance will be<span class='line-break'> </span>improved. If the fence is removed the only<span class='line-break'> </span>expense will be for cleaning the headstones ($5).</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering <span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
<p><date when='1883-08-30'>Aug 30<sup>th</sup> [188]3</date></p>
<p>Mrs Susan H. Page</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>To grade &amp; sod<span class='line-break'> </span>lot #1775 on Hibiscus Path will cost<span class='line-break'> </span>($44<sup rend='sup'>00</sup>) forty four dollars.</p>
<p>The myrtle on the lot both on the<span class='line-break'> </span>border &amp; the graves needs very consid<span class='line-break'></span>erable repairs. <p>M<sup>r</sup>. J.R. Poor who<span class='line-break'> </span>owns a lot in M<sup>t</sup>. <p>Should the Corporation take the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot in exchange I desire to know<span class='line-break'> </span>whether you would not care, either<span class='line-break'> </span>for some member of your family or for<span class='line-break'> </span>some friend, to become the purchaser<span class='line-break'> </span>as it seems to me that you are interested<span class='line-break'> </span>more in the matter than any one else.</p>
<p>Should it be taken in exchange<span class='line-break'> </span>and then come into the hands of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Corporation it is quite probable<span class='line-break'> </span>that the granite coping would be <span class='line-break'> </span>removed off of the portions which<span class='line-break'> </span>they bought as the land would be<span class='line-break'> </span>more saleable in a separate lot without<span class='line-break'> </span>a curbing. In this event some<span class='line-break'> </span>arrangement could be made<span class='line-break'> </span>with you for completing the curbing<span class='line-break'> </span>around your portion of the enclosure<span class='line-break'> </span>if you desired.</p>

<p>J.W. Lovering <span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

Brown<span class='line-break'> </span>(#192 on Violet Path) which you<span class='line-break'> </span>now represent and it would<span class='line-break'> </span>seem to me that certain changes<span class='line-break'> </span>could be made in your lot<span class='line-break'> </span>which would improve the appear<span class='line-break'></span>ance of your lot very much, as<span class='line-break'> </span>well as the general surroundings,<span class='line-break'> </span>so that I take the liberty to suggest<span class='line-break'> </span>that the fence be removed, and that<span class='line-break'> </span>the grade of the lot be raised in<span class='line-break'> </span>the rear to the height at which<span class='line-break'> </span>the top rail now stands, and that<span class='line-break'> </span>the surface of the lot be regraded<span class='line-break'> </span>so as to slope forward from the<span class='line-break'> </span>back of the lot, raised as explained<span class='line-break'> </span>above, to the front which should be<span class='line-break'> </span>not over a foot lower than now.</p>
<p>If this regrading were done, it<span class='line-break'> </span>would be possible to make the<span class='line-break'> </span>path on the N. side of the lot more<span class='line-break'> </span>gradual and would much improve<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157738">CB06_0509</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-10-17'>Oct. 17<sup>th</sup> [188]3.</date></p>
<p>Geo. Thacher Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In reply to <span class='line-break'> </span>your favor of the 16<sup>th</sup>. I would say<span class='line-break'> </span>that the removal of your mother's<span class='line-break'> </span>remains can take place at such<span class='line-break'> </span>time as you prefer, if you give<span class='line-break'> </span>several days notice of the time<span class='line-break'> </span>desired, and should it prove to<span class='line-break'> </span>be a stormy day, the removal can<span class='line-break'> </span>be postponed to the first pleasant<span class='line-break'> </span>day at the same hour. When you<span class='line-break'> </span>decide, will you please insert the<span class='line-break'> </span>day &amp; hour &amp; sign the enclosed blank<span class='line-break'> </span>and return to me, and please<span class='line-break'> </span>state at same time, whether a<span class='line-break'> </span>brick vault is to be placed in the<span class='line-break'> </span>new lot for your mother's remains, &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>if it is to be on the right hand ^<sup>(as you face the lot)</sup> side<span class='line-break'> </span>of your father's grave which is the<span class='line-break'> </span>usual place.</p>
<p>The brick grave can be prepared &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>the grave in the old lot opened so<span class='line-break'> </span>that when you reach here you<span class='line-break'> </span>would find every thing ready to<span class='line-break'> </span>have the transfer made in a <span class='line-break'> </span>short time.</p>
<p>Under the circumstances, I think<span class='line-break'> </span>the old stone might be removed, but<span class='line-break'> </span>it should be set as low as possible.<span class='line-break'> </span>No shrub of any kind would be<span class='line-break'> </span>allowed as a hedge or mark around<span class='line-break'> </span>your lot, but myrtle or annual<span class='line-break'> </span>flowers can be planted, but <span class='line-break'> </span>when in straight lines, I think</p>
<p>509</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157739">
<h3><a name="page-1157739">CB06_0510</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>result is too stiff to look well<span class='line-break'> </span>and I would suggest that a <span class='line-break'> </span>bed for flowers be cut at each<span class='line-break'> </span>corner post, in which you could<span class='line-break'> </span>have either mixed flowering annuals<span class='line-break'> </span>or foliage plants as you prefer.</p>
<p>You may see better what I mean<span class='line-break'> </span>by the rough sketch below.</p>
<p>[Diagram: small sketch showing corner posts &amp; flower beds with Fountain Ave at bottom of sketch]</p>
<p>The four beds<span class='line-break'> </span>marked "F" <span class='line-break'> </span>for flowers.</p>
<p>The lot directly back of yours has<span class='line-break'> </span>a myrtle border, and I think by<span class='line-break'> </span>contrast that the arrangement<span class='line-break'> </span>which I suggest would look<span class='line-break'> </span>better.</p>
<p>As the lot is a large one, a shrub<span class='line-break'> </span>might be planted at each corner in<span class='line-break'> </span>place of the annuals, if you prefer.</p>
<p>Yours very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>510</p>
</div>

<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-11-19'>Nov 19<sup>th</sup>/ [188]3.</date></p>
<p>John R. Poor Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In reply to your<span class='line-break'> </span>favor of the 17<sup rend='sup'>th</sup>/ inst I would say<span class='line-break'> </span>that I have named as low a<span class='line-break'> </span>sum for grading the lots (3119 &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>4390 on Caltha Path) as the work<span class='line-break'> </span>can be well done for, and that in<span class='line-break'> </span>making my estimate, I have al<span class='line-break'></span>lowed a much larger amount of<span class='line-break'> </span>loam than you do which accounts<span class='line-break'> </span>for a considerable difference. I found<span class='line-break'> </span>too that the sods around the mon<span class='line-break'></span>ument were so much damaged in<span class='line-break'> </span>putting up the monument, that sev<span class='line-break'></span>eral hundred square feet of new sod<span class='line-break'> </span>would have to be supplied, to<span class='line-break'> </span>take the place of the waste in cutting<span class='line-break'> </span>and that which could not be [stripped?]</p>
<p>I should be glad to have<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot placed under perpetual care<span class='line-break'> </span>but I could not accept $400 with<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot in its present condition.</p>
<p>It has always been customary<span class='line-break'> </span>for proprietors to put their lots<span class='line-break'> </span>in good order and to the grade<span class='line-break'> </span>at which they were to be left,<span class='line-break'> </span>at their own expense in addition<span class='line-break'> </span>to the amount named for the<span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care, and every purchaser<span class='line-break'> </span>of a lot receives a separate bill<span class='line-break'> </span>for the grading &amp; sodding &amp;c of his<span class='line-break'> </span>lot at the time of payment for<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<p>In regard to your<span class='line-break'> </span>claim for an abatement of [$16?]<span class='line-break'> </span>because of the renewal of the<span class='line-break'> </span>fence. The difference in the <span class='line-break'> </span>estimate was made on the supposition<span class='line-break'> </span>that the work would be all done<span class='line-break'> </span>at the same time. You can see<span class='line-break'> </span>how much quicker the workman<span class='line-break'> </span>could have done this work if the<span class='line-break'> </span>fence had not been there to impede<span class='line-break'> </span>them and if they had not to carry<span class='line-break'> </span>all their material in at one<span class='line-break'> </span>narrow gate. Then in now renewing<span class='line-break'> </span>the fence and taking up the posts<span class='line-break'> </span>we will destroy part of the sod just<span class='line-break'> </span>laid. All the credit that could be<span class='line-break'> </span>allowed would be $2. The work<span class='line-break'> </span>has not yet been done and under <span class='line-break'> </span>these circumstances do you decire it<span class='line-break'> </span>to go on.</p>

<p>Richard H. Salter M.D.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have measured<span class='line-break'> </span>this afternoon the change of<span class='line-break'> </span>grade of the path in front of<span class='line-break'> </span>your lot, and find it has been<span class='line-break'> </span>lowered thirteen inches, and I<span class='line-break'> </span>find that the lot is about a<span class='line-break'> </span>foot above the adjoining lots,<span class='line-break'> </span>so that if the grade of the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>is not changed at all, it will<span class='line-break'> </span>be about two feet above the<span class='line-break'> </span>path, and if the grade is low<span class='line-break'></span>ered to conform to that of the<span class='line-break'> </span>adjoining lots, the lot will be<span class='line-break'> </span>just as much above the changed<span class='line-break'> </span>path, as the lot (as now) graded<span class='line-break'> </span>was above the [Ave?] path.</p>
<p>In regard to the expense of the<span class='line-break'> </span>changes, I am disposed to do<span class='line-break'> </span>what is fair, as you feel that<span class='line-break'> </span>you are rather compelled to make<span class='line-break'> </span>the change.</p>
<p>I will regrade the lot, lowering<span class='line-break'> </span>the surface about a foot, to con<span class='line-break'></span>form to the adjoining lots, using<span class='line-break'> </span>over the same sod now on the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>without expense to you, or if you<span class='line-break'> </span>desire a new turf, I will<span class='line-break'> </span>make the change &amp; supply the new<span class='line-break'> </span>sod for $20.</p>
<p>Please let me hear your decision<span class='line-break'> </span>soon, as it is getting late in the <span class='line-break'> </span>season, &amp; it is desirable that the work<span class='line-break'> </span>should go on.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157774">CB06_0545</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-13-18'>Dec<sup>r</sup> 18<sup>th</sup> [188]3</date></p>
<p>Messrs Wittemore Bros.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs</p>
<p>Your favor of the<span class='line-break'> </span>17<sup>th</sup> is received also copy of the<span class='line-break'> </span>album.</p>
<p>I have only had time to<span class='line-break'> </span>give it a hasty examination<span class='line-break'> </span>but think it will prove satisfac<span class='line-break'></span>tory.</p>
<p>I notice however that the Bowditch<span class='line-break'> </span>Monument &amp; the Lawrence mont.<span class='line-break'> </span>are misplaced, as far as the names<span class='line-break'> </span>underneath all catacombs.</p>
<p>If all the copies are printed, cannot<span class='line-break'> </span>some later reference be arranged<span class='line-break'> </span>so as to correct this mistake?</p>
<p>By a letter over the view, <span class='line-break'> </span>a corresponding one below at<span class='line-break'> </span>the proper title - this might be done<span class='line-break'> </span>or pehaps you can make some<span class='line-break'> </span>suggestion, but it would be<span class='line-break'> </span>a pity to have it go out<span class='line-break'> </span>wrongly marked without correction.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>545</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1157775">
<h3><a name="page-1157775">CB06_0546</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1883-12-20'>December 20<sup>th</sup>/ [188]3</date></p>
<p>Messrs Wittemann Bros.<span class='line-break'> </span>New York.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs</p>
<p>I am in receipt<span class='line-break'> </span>of your favor of Dec. 19<sup>th</sup>/. &amp; have noted<span class='line-break'> </span>contents.</p>
<p>I have talked with our printer<span class='line-break'> </span>in regard to the corporation of the mistake<span class='line-break'> </span>in the album (in the transposition of the<span class='line-break'> </span>names Lawrence &amp; Bowditch) and find<span class='line-break'> </span>that he is unwilling to undertake the<span class='line-break'> </span>job with any assurance that it will<span class='line-break'> </span>be done neatly &amp; satisfactorily, so that I<span class='line-break'> </span>cannot do otherwise than reship the<span class='line-break'> </span>books to you.</p>
<p>I am willing that the books should be<span class='line-break'> </span>corrected, if it can be done, in a<span class='line-break'> </span>neat &amp; workman like manner, and<span class='line-break'> </span>would prefer to have the book without<span class='line-break'> </span>this view rather than to have it repaired<span class='line-break'> </span>in a careless way, this in latter case I<span class='line-break'> </span>think an allowance should be made<span class='line-break'> </span>for the ^<sup>reduction in</sup> size of the book.</p>
<p>I do not wish to dictate in any way<span class='line-break'> </span>as to how the book had better be<span class='line-break'> </span>repaired, for you are better judges of<span class='line-break'> </span>that than I -- but it should be <u>neatly</u><span class='line-break'> </span>corrected in some way before the books<span class='line-break'> </span>are returned to me.</p>
<p>I regret also to have found another<span class='line-break'> </span>error in the printing of Sumner's name<span class='line-break'> </span>which is printed Sum<u>m</u>er instead of<span class='line-break'> </span>Sumner, but this error I think you can<span class='line-break'> </span>correct with a pen knife.</p>
<p>Both for your own sake &amp; mine I</p>
<p>546</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

They do<span class='line-break'> </span>not seem to be very vigorous &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>perhaps the deutzias would be<span class='line-break'> </span>better, but I fear that the oak<span class='line-break'> </span>trees which are near enough to<span class='line-break'> </span>shade the lot, will prevent them<span class='line-break'> </span>or anything else from doing as<span class='line-break'> </span>well, as they would in another<span class='line-break'> </span>and more favorable situation.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157792">CB06_0563</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1884-01-30'>Jan 30 [188]4</date></p>
<p>Waldron H Rand Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Ass't Treas Boston Univ</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Yours of yesterday<span class='line-break'> </span>is received. Similar notices are<span class='line-break'> </span>usually sent to all proprietors whose<span class='line-break'> </span>addresses are known.</p>
<p>The Trustees desire as far as possible to<span class='line-break'> </span>keep the care of lots under their<span class='line-break'> </span>own charge. The number they care<span class='line-break'> </span>for has advanced until only about<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>1</sup>/10 of the whole and cared for by<span class='line-break'> </span>others than the employees of the Corporation.<span class='line-break'> </span>This has enabled the Trustees to reduce<span class='line-break'> </span>the charges so that the care and<span class='line-break'> </span>top dressing of a 300 foot lot formerly<span class='line-break'> </span>charged $9 is now but $5<sup>00</sup> and any<span class='line-break'> </span>profit which may result, in a favorable<span class='line-break'> </span>year is suspended on the general<span class='line-break'> </span>improvement of the grounds and<span class='line-break'> </span>not for the advantage of any individ<span class='line-break'> </span>-ual.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>pr</sup> J.C.S. <span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<p>The Corporation would not desire<span class='line-break'> </span>to become the purchaser at any<span class='line-break'> </span>price, and at this season of the<span class='line-break'> </span>year, there are very few lot sales.<span class='line-break'> </span>If there were no burials in the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>it would bring <sup rend='sup'>$</sup>400 to <sup rend='sup'>$</sup>450 but with<span class='line-break'> </span>the burials then it would not be<span class='line-break'> </span>likely to bring at the same rate even<span class='line-break'> </span>for the space unoccupied.</p>

<div id="page-1157808">
<h3><a name="page-1157808">CB06_0579</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1884-02-21'>Feby 21<sup rend='sup'>st</sup> [188]4</date></p>
<p>Mrs R C Stanfield<span class='line-break'> </span>New York</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>Mr Mackintosh<span class='line-break'> </span>our Treasurer has handed me your<span class='line-break'> </span>letter for answer. You ordered your<span class='line-break'> </span>marbles cleaned in July. You again<span class='line-break'> </span>ordered them cleaned in Sept, both<span class='line-break'> </span>the orders are on file at this office.</p>
<p>The charges are not alike in amount<span class='line-break'> </span>because the time spent on the work was<span class='line-break'> </span>greater at one time than the other.</p>
<p>You brought one of your bills in to this<span class='line-break'> </span>office but this not being the Treasurers<span class='line-break'> </span>office we had no means of knowing<span class='line-break'> </span>how your account stood just then.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span><sup rend='sup'>per</sup>J.C.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup't</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157815">CB06_0586</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1884-03-14'>Mch 14<sup>th</sup> [188]4</date></p>
<p>Mrs George W. Hammond</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>I would<span class='line-break'> </span>say in regard to the cover of the<span class='line-break'> </span>monument, that it is not in our<span class='line-break'> </span>possession and never has been.</p>
<p>It was furnished originally and put <span class='line-break'> </span>in by parties from Boston I think,<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] after it blew over, it was<span class='line-break'> </span>[put?] up again (to prevent additional<span class='line-break'> </span>damage) by our workmen here, and<span class='line-break'> </span>in that time has not, to the best<span class='line-break'> </span>of my knowledge been put up again.<span class='line-break'> </span>It was removed by the same parties<span class='line-break'> </span>I think who put it up, at any rate<span class='line-break'> </span>it is not and has not been in<span class='line-break'> </span>our care and the contract for the<span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care makes no provision<span class='line-break'> </span>for the covering of the monument.</p>
<p>It is customary to specify this<span class='line-break'> </span>in the contract when there is a <span class='line-break'> </span>covering to be put on.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>586</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p><date when='1884-03-26'>Mch. 26<sup>th</sup> [188]4</date></p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I find that there will be<span class='line-break'> </span>fifty linear feet of hedge to<span class='line-break'> </span>be set out to take the place of<span class='line-break'> </span>that now there, and that when<span class='line-break'> </span>the present hedge is taken away<span class='line-break'> </span>some sodding would be very desir<span class='line-break'></span>able on the banks in the rear of<span class='line-break'> </span>the hedge.</p>
<p>The whole cost of the hedge<span class='line-break'> </span>(the plants to be 18 to 20 inches high)<span class='line-break'> </span>and sodding, including some special<span class='line-break'> </span>care in the way of watering which<span class='line-break'> </span>would be necessary for the first<span class='line-break'> </span>season, would be forty five dollars.</p>
<p>The Frothingham lot is under<span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care, so that for that<span class='line-break'> </span>portion of the hedge, we should<span class='line-break'> </span>receive payment from the fund,<span class='line-break'> </span>leaving $22<sup>50</sup> to be paid by the<span class='line-break'> </span>owners of the other lot.</p>
<p>As soon as you deside when<span class='line-break'> </span>you will have the scarlet^<sup>variety </sup> or not.<span class='line-break'> </span>please advise me, that I may<span class='line-break'> </span>order the plants.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
<p>Roger Wolcott Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>P.S. I neglected to say, that I<span class='line-break'> </span>think the scarlet variety makes<span class='line-break'> </span>rather the best hedge, tho' the blossoms<span class='line-break'> </span>of the pink &amp; white, is more beautiful.</p>

<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>I think the matter<span class='line-break'> </span>of the addition to the Earle lot<span class='line-break'> </span>could be best arranged on the<span class='line-break'> </span>ground and if you are likely to<span class='line-break'> </span>be here again, it would be the<span class='line-break'> </span>more satisfactory way, but I will<span class='line-break'> </span>explain as clearly as I can by [letter?]</p>
<p>An addition of two and one<span class='line-break'> </span>half feet can be sold on the<span class='line-break'> </span>right hand side of the lot. (as you<span class='line-break'> </span>stand on the Avenue facing the lot)<span class='line-break'> </span>but there is a difficulty in the<span class='line-break'> </span>way of adding more, which is</p>
<p>caused by the banking at the rear<span class='line-break'> </span>sloping [so..?] to the lots below.</p>
<p>I find that there is not room for<span class='line-break'> </span>this bank, if an addition of greater<span class='line-break'> </span>width should be sold, but there is<span class='line-break'> </span>one way in which it might be<span class='line-break'> </span>done. The headstones on the back<span class='line-break'> </span>line of your lot do not set back<span class='line-break'> </span>as far as the near line of the lot, and<span class='line-break'> </span>if you were willing to have this<span class='line-break'> </span>line moved forward so as to touch<span class='line-break'> </span>the bases of the headstones then I<span class='line-break'> </span>think an addition might be sold<span class='line-break'> </span>between five and six feet in width<span class='line-break'> </span>providing the owners of the adjoining<span class='line-break'> </span>lot do not wish to purchase any<span class='line-break'> </span>part of it themselves.</p>
<p>I could explain the whole matter<span class='line-break'> </span>to you on the grounds in a few minutes</p>
<p>Yrs truly</p>
<p>J W Lovering</p>
<p>623</p>

<p>Since writing<span class='line-break'> </span>you in regard to the Longfellow<span class='line-break'> </span>monument, I have learned that<span class='line-break'> </span>the makers marked the line on<span class='line-break'> </span>the monument showing the height<span class='line-break'> </span>on the base above the sod, and that<span class='line-break'> </span>it was necessary in order to set it<span class='line-break'> </span>to the mark to fill in again [?]<span class='line-break'> </span>if not all of the foundation which<span class='line-break'> </span>was taken off after the foundation<span class='line-break'> </span>was built in accordance with your<span class='line-break'> </span>instructions.</p>
<p>Under the condition of things, there</p>
<p>can be no difficulty in lowering<span class='line-break'> </span>the whole monument, without [taking?]<span class='line-break'> </span>it down, four inches and I think this<span class='line-break'> </span>will be less expensive than raising<span class='line-break'> </span>the grade &amp; trust it may meet <span class='line-break'> </span>with your approval.</p>
<p>The cost will not exceed $25<sup>00</sup> and<span class='line-break'> </span>may not [excuse?] $20<sup>00</sup>. I have had<span class='line-break'> </span>such work done before successfully<span class='line-break'> </span>and it can be completed within<span class='line-break'> </span>two or three days.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering<sub>Supt.</sub></p>
<p>695</p>

<h3><a name="page-1157950">CB06_0722</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>June 30th [188]4</p>
<p>Brice S Evans Esq.</p>
<p>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your note is received</p>
<p>I am sorry you did not find your<span class='line-break'> </span>lot in a satisfactory condition The<span class='line-break'> </span>land is high there and it is hard<span class='line-break'> </span>to make grass do well. The gardener<span class='line-break'> </span>has not changed bed for flowers as<span class='line-break'> </span>you think the only new places opened<span class='line-break'> </span>being the graves as you ordered<span class='line-break'> </span>Grass seed was sown all over the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>this spring and I will see that it is<span class='line-break'> </span>done again in fall - It would<span class='line-break'> </span>cost <sup>$</sup>50 to have the lot graded and</p>
<p>sodded and $25 more [?] curbing<span class='line-break'> </span>right -</p>
<p>When in the office the other day you spoke<span class='line-break'> </span>of lowering the lot. If the curbing and 3<span class='line-break'> </span>steps were removed the lot could be lowered<span class='line-break'> </span>3 to 4 ft. The work. including regrading<span class='line-break'> </span>and sodding could be done for $130 and<span class='line-break'> </span>the old stone</p>
<p>Very respectfully</p>
<p>JW Lovering<sub>Supt</sub></p>
<p><sup>pr</sup>J.C.S.</p>
<p>722</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157951">
<h3><a name="page-1157951">CB06_0723</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>June 30th [188]4</p>
<p>Messrs Geo. Sevins &amp; Son</p>
<p>Worcester</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your note is received<span class='line-break'> </span>enclosing orders properly signed - The<span class='line-break'> </span>permits you have to get in your own<span class='line-break'> </span>name from the City Clerk of Cambridge</p>
<p>In coming here you will pass the City<span class='line-break'> </span>Hall so that you will have no delay</p>
<p>Let me know what day you will<span class='line-break'> </span>come and I will have the graves<span class='line-break'> </span>opened</p>
<p>Very respectfully</p>
<p>JW Lovering</p>
<p><sup>pr</sup>J.C.S Supt</p>
<p>June 30th [188]4</p>
<p>Alvin Hayes Esq.</p>
<p>Cambridgeport</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In regard to the Carter<span class='line-break'> </span>lot #1234. The perpetual care of the<span class='line-break'> </span>grass and cleaning of the monument<span class='line-break'> </span>will cost $125 the lot at first to be put<span class='line-break'> </span>in order.</p>
<p>To cut down posts cut the number<span class='line-break'> </span>and grade and sod the lot will<span class='line-break'> </span>cost $36~</p>
<p>Very respectfully</p>
<p>JW Lovering</p>
<p><sup>pr</sup>J.C.S.</p>
<p>Supt</p>
<p>723</p>
</div>

<div class="page-content">
<p>July 2<sup>nd</sup> [188]4.</p>
<p>W.A. Haskell Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The spaceway between<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot #327 (Robinson) and the adjoining<span class='line-break'> </span>lots seem to be needed for the terraces<span class='line-break'> </span>which [?] the different grades<span class='line-break'> </span>of the lots, so that it does not seem<span class='line-break'> </span>practical to make an addition<span class='line-break'> </span>to the lot.</p>
<p>Yrs truly</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering<sub>Supt.</sub></p>
<p>725</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1157954">
<h3><a name="page-1157954">CB06_0726</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>July 2<sup>nd</sup> [188]4</p>
<p>H.B. Mackintosh Treas<sup>r.</sup></p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>There are to be<span class='line-break'> </span>some repairs made on greenhouses<span class='line-break'> </span>connected with the brick boiler house<span class='line-break'> </span>known as Nos. 4,5,6, the sills, ridge &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>some of the rafters requiring renewal<span class='line-break'> </span>and the work will probably be spread<span class='line-break'> </span>over the next month, during which<span class='line-break'> </span>time there will be no plants in the <span class='line-break'> </span>houses.</p>
<p>There will be little, if any work, re<span class='line-break'></span>quiring any fine for the workmen.</p>
<p>Will you please send the insurance<span class='line-break'> </span>policy with the statement, to the</p>
<p>agents and obtain the necessary permit<span class='line-break'> </span>that the policy may not be violated<span class='line-break'> </span>in any way.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering<sub>Supt.</sub></p>
<p>726<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1157955">CB06_0727</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
</div>

<div id="page-1157956">
<h3><a name="page-1157956">CB06_0728</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>July 8<sup>th</sup> [188]4</p>
<p>G. Quincy Thorndike Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your note is received<span class='line-break'> </span>An examination of the ground shows<span class='line-break'> </span>the sketch you sent to be correct. By our<span class='line-break'> </span>records [Josepha?] &amp; [Perdis?] Hill are buried<span class='line-break'> </span>in your lot but this is probably a mistake</p>
<p>Two additional rows of brick graves<span class='line-break'> </span>could probably be built but I do not<span class='line-break'> </span>think there is room for more than<span class='line-break'> </span>8 in a row. Brick graves for future <span class='line-break'> </span>use cost <sup>$</sup>18-- each</p>
<p>Two interments can be made<span class='line-break'> </span>in one grave provided the upper</p>
<p>one is 3 ft below surface.</p>
<p>I doubt if the graves now there<span class='line-break'> </span>are deep enough to permit inter<span class='line-break'></span>ments being over them</p>
<p>Very respectfully</p>
<p>J W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>per</sup>J.C.S.</p>
<p>[in pencil]<span class='line-break'> </span>It would not be well to build<span class='line-break'> </span>the brick graves until fall<span class='line-break'> </span>working there <sup>in the hot weather</sup> would<span class='line-break'> </span>require [new?] sodding.</p>
<p>728</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1157957">
<h3><a name="page-1157957">CB06_0729</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>July 9 [188]4</p>
<p>Alfred Merrill Esq</p>
<p>Cambridge</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Mr McArthur has<span class='line-break'> </span>handed in the enclosed bill to be returned<span class='line-break'> </span>to you. He says the sod looks well<span class='line-break'> </span>except around the corners of curbing and<span class='line-break'> </span>around headstones and monument</p>
<p>Two small headstones are out of plumb<span class='line-break'> </span>and should be righted. And the<span class='line-break'> </span>statue should be cleaned. The <span class='line-break'> </span>expense of all this would be<span class='line-break'> </span>about $6~</p>
<p>3642.</p>
<p>Very respectfully</p>
<p>JW Lovering<sub>Supt</sub></p>
<p><sup>pr</sup>J.C.S.</p>
<p>July 9th [188]4</p>
<p>Mrs B.F. Shattuck</p>
<p>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>Your note is<span class='line-break'> </span>received. I very much regret the<span class='line-break'> </span>trouble and annoyance the bodiees<span class='line-break'> </span>were subject to. It appears that<span class='line-break'> </span>the gate keeper made a mistake as<span class='line-break'> </span>to the funeral - I am glad<span class='line-break'> </span>you called my attention to the matter<span class='line-break'> </span>as it will prevent a recurrence of the<span class='line-break'> </span>same thing - We have an order for the care<span class='line-break'> </span>of your lot until countermanded so that a<span class='line-break'> </span>circular did not need to be sent. The<span class='line-break'> </span>cleaning etc will have attention</p>
<p>Very respectfully</p>
<p>JW Lovering</p>
<p><sup>pr</sup>J.C.S.</p>
<p>729</p>
</div>
